Understanding Obligations in Logic: Collective vs Individual
Explanation of obligation degrees in learning logic.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between individual obligation (wajib 'ayn) and collective obligation (wajib kifaya) as applied to the study of logic.

Core Idea
Logic's obligation varies: essential part is individual, further study is collective.

Muslim scholars debated whether learning logic is obligatory, recommended, or something else. The second opinion presented here introduces a nuanced view: the essential amount of logic is an individual duty, while additional study is a collective responsibility. This distinction is common in Islamic jurisprudence and has practical implications for how we prioritize learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of obligation mentioned
Find the terms 'wujub kifaya' (collective obligation) and 'wajib 'ayn' (individual obligation) in the passage. Note that the author says some scholars made logic absolutely obligatory, while others said it is a collective obligation.
The terms are in the Arabic: وجوب الكفاية and وجوب العين (implied).
2
Understand the scope of each obligation
The passage specifies that the 'essential amount' (al-qadr al-daruri) of logic is an individual obligation, meaning every Muslim must learn at least that much. What exceeds that is a collective obligation, meaning if some learn it, the rest are absolved.
This is similar to how fard 'ayn and fard kifaya work in fiqh.
3
Connect to the authority cited
The author credits Imam al-Ghazali with this view. Al-Ghazali famously stated that one without logic cannot be trusted with his knowledge, emphasizing logic's foundational role for the Islamic sciences.
Al-Ghazali's position is found in his work 'al-Mustasfa'.
4
Apply the distinction to other Islamic sciences
Think of how other sciences are categorized: learning the basics of salah is individual obligation, while advanced fiqh is collective. Similarly, logic has a basic level that everyone needs for sound reasoning, and advanced levels for specialists.
This shows integration of logic into the Islamic curriculum.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الرأي الثاني: بعض العلماء أوجبوا علم المنطق مطلقا). وقال بعضهم: يجب على الناس وجوب كفاية أن يعلموا المنطق، وهذا الرأي أخصُّ من الإيجاب مطلقاً، لأنه إيجاب على سبيل الكفاية، كسائر العلوم الإسلامية، وقد يُفْهَمُ من كلامهم مجردُ نَدْبِهِ ولصاحب هذا الرأي أن يُفَضِّلَ فيقول : القدر الضروري من المنطق واجب وجوب عين، وما زاد على ذلك فهو واجب وجوب كفاية . والإمام الغزالي هو من تصدى لإثبات هذا القول وصرح به في أوائل (6).. (5) (4)
The second opinion: Some scholars made the science of logic absolutely obligatory. And some said: it is a collective obligation on people to learn logic. This opinion is more specific than absolute obligation, because it is an obligation by way of sufficiency (kifaya), like other Islamic sciences. And from their words, mere recommendation (nadb) may be understood. The proponent of this opinion may specify and say: the essential amount of logic is an individual obligation, and what exceeds that is a collective obligation. Imam al-Ghazali is the one who undertook to prove this statement and declared it in the beginnings [of his works] (4). (5) (6)
Source pages p. 10

Commentary
This passage presents the second opinion regarding the ruling on studying logic. It distinguishes between absolute obligation (wujub mutlaq) and collective obligation (wujub kifaya). Some scholars view logic as a collective duty like other Islamic sciences. There is also a nuance: the essential part of logic is an individual obligation, while additional study is a collective obligation. The author attributes this view to Imam al-Ghazali, who stated that one who has no knowledge of logic cannot be trusted with his knowledge. The footnotes (4), (5), (6) elaborate on the two situations for individual obligation and the necessity of logic for defending the faith, though the text is incomplete.

Key Terms
وجوب الكفاية
القدر الضروري
الإمام الغزالي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second opinion, what is the ruling on the essential amount of logic?
A) It is completely forbidden.
B) It is a collective obligation.
C) It is an individual obligation.
D) It is merely recommended.

Key Takeaway
The essential part of logic is personally obligatory for every Muslim, while advanced study is a collective responsibility.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the knowledge of tajweed (Quranic recitation). Is learning the basic rules of tajweed an individual or collective obligation? Use the same reasoning from the passage to categorize it.
?
Identify a contemporary Islamic science (e.g., ʿulūm al-ḥadīth). Which part of it would you classify as 'essential amount' and thus individually obligatory?

The Three Means of Knowledge: Sense, Intellect, and Report
Author classifies the three means of human knowledge and explains the importance of transmitted report.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify the three means of human knowledge according to Islamic epistemology and explain the relationship between sense and intellect, and the unique role of transmitted report.

Core Idea
Knowledge comes from sense, intellect, and report; report is the key to divine knowledge.

In this passage, the author presents the foundational classification of the sources of human knowledge. Understanding these three means is crucial for recognizing how we attain certainty in Islamic sciences. The senses provide raw data, the intellect processes it, and transmitted report (khabar) delivers knowledge beyond direct experience—especially about Allah, the unseen, and divine commands.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three means named
Read the passage and list the three means of knowledge explicitly mentioned: al-hiss (sense), al-'aql (intellect), and al-khabar (transmitted report).
The text says 'three, no fourth'.
2
Distinguish independent from composed means
Note that senses and intellect are described as independent (mustaqillatan), while khabar is composed (murakkab) from them. Understand that 'independent' means neither is built from the other, though they may rely on each other in some way.
The author stresses that senses and intellect are not composed from each other.
3
Analyze the condition vs cause distinction
The commentary explains that sense is a condition (shart) for the intellect, not a cause ('illa). This means the intellect depends on sense to start, but once it has data, it can function even without ongoing sensory input. Look for the phrase 'not a cause' in the translation.
This distinction is subtle: a condition enables, but a cause produces.
4
Recognize why khabar is singled out
Despite being composed, khabar is given special mention because it is a vast source of knowledge. The text lists what we learn via khabar: attributes of God, creation stories, destiny, divine commands, and moral perfection. This underscores its importance in Islamic theology.
Khabar is the medium for revealed knowledge.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وسائل المعرفة: وسائل العلم والمعرفة الإنسانية هي ثلاث لا رابع لها، وسيلتان مستقلتان لا يتركب واحد منهما من الآخر، وإن اعتمد عليه بوجه والثالث مركب منهما ، ولكن أفرد بالذكر لأهميته.
(1) الوسيلتان المستقلتان اللتان لا يتركب أحدهما من الآخر هما الحس والعقل . قوله ( وإن اعتمد عليه بوجـه) أى وإن اعتمد أحدهما على الآخر بوجه ما يشير إلى أن الحس شرط للعقل، وتنبه إلى أن الحس ليس علـه للعقل، فبعد وقوع الشرط، يبقى العقل يعمل حتى وإن انقطع الحس. والثالث المركب من الحس والعقل وهـو طريق الخبر ، لأنّ وصوله إلى النفس يكون من طريق الحواس، وإدراكه وفهمه والحكم على صحته وبطلانـــه وجوازه كل ذلك يكون بالعقل. فافهم. وأما أهمية الخبر التي لأجلها أفرده بالذكر مع كونه مركباً فهى كونه مصدراً هائلاً من مصادر المعرفة، وبهذه الوسيلة الشريفة تعرفنا على صفات الإله، وعرفنا أصل خلقتنا وأخبارنا الماضية، ومآلنا، والوظيفة المنوطة بنا في هذه الحياة، وعرفنا أوامر الإله جلّ وعز ونواهيه، وكيف نترقى فــي كمالاتنا، إلخ مما لا حصر من المعارف.
The means of knowledge: The means of human knowledge and cognition are three, no fourth, two independent means, neither composed from the other, although one relies on the other in some way, and the third is composed from them, but it is singled out for its importance. (1) The two independent means that are not composed from each other are sense and intellect. His statement (although it relies on the other in some way) means that sense is a condition for the intellect, and he alerts that sense is not a cause for the intellect, so after the condition occurs, the intellect continues to work even if sense is cut off. The third, composed of sense and intellect, is the way of transmitted report (khabar), because its arrival to the soul is through the senses, and its perception, understanding, and judgment on its correctness, falsehood, and permissibility are all by the intellect. Understand. As for the importance of khabar for which it was singled out despite being composed: it is that it is a tremendous source of knowledge. By this noble means we come to know the attributes of God, and we know the origin of our creation, our past reports, our final destiny, the function assigned to us in this life, and we know the commands and prohibitions of God Almighty, and how we ascend in our perfections, etc., of countless knowledges.
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage defines the three means of human knowledge. The author begins by stating that there are exactly three: two independent and one composed. The independent means are the senses and the intellect; the composed means is transmitted report (khabar). The commentary explains that the senses are a condition for the intellect, not a cause – the intellect can work even after the senses are cut off. Khabar is composed because it involves sense perception of the report and intellectual judgment of its content. The passage highlights the immense importance of khabar, especially for religious knowledge: through it we learn about God, creation, destiny, and divine commands. This underscores why khabar is singled out despite being derived from the other two.

Key Terms
الحس
العقل
الخبر

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following best describes the relationship between sense and intellect?
A) Sense is a cause of intellect.
B) Sense is a condition for intellect.
C) Intellect is independent of sense.
D) Sense and intellect are both independent and not related.

Key Takeaway
The three means of knowledge are sense, intellect, and transmitted report, with report being the primary vehicle for divine knowledge.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
1. Read the passage and list an example from Islamic law where all three means of knowledge are used together (e.g., determining the time of prayer based on sighting, reasoning, and authoritative report).
?
2. Explain in your own words why the author says sense is a condition but not a cause for intellect, using a concrete example from kalam (e.g., knowing the existence of God through intellectual proof after observing the world through senses).

The Five Senses and the Nature of Perception
Author describes the five senses, the mechanism of perception, and the limitations of sensory knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish direct from indirect perception and explain why sensory perception is incomplete according to Islamic logicians.

Core Idea
Perception only grasps partial properties, never the full reality.

The passage before you explores the five senses and the mechanics of perception. It clarifies that the senses only perceive what is connected to them, either directly (touch) or through an intermediary (sight via reflected rays). More importantly, it reveals a fundamental limitation: our perception never captures the object as it truly is, only some of its inseparable concomitant properties. This insight is crucial for understanding how Islamic logicians view the relationship between the senses, the intellect, and knowledge.

Guided Path
1
Identify the five senses and their common feature
Locate the list of the five senses: hearing, sight, taste, touch, and smell. Note the statement that they only perceive what is connected to them. This connection can be direct (mubashara) or indirect (wasita).
The common feature is the necessity of connection between sense and object.
2
Distinguish direct vs indirect connection
Find the terms 'mubashara' (direct) and 'wasita' (indirect). Touch is given as an example of direct perception; sight via reflected rays is an example of indirect perception. Understand that in indirect perception, an intermediary (e.g., the ray) is directly connected to the sense, not the object itself.
This distinction is central to the discussion of what exactly is perceived.
3
Analyze the debate about what sight perceives
The passage presents two views: (a) sight perceives the body itself via a ray connecting to it, or (b) sight perceives only the reflected ray. Which view does the author prefer and why? The author favors (b) because the ray is directly connected to the eye, whereas the body is not. This illustrates the principle that a sense only perceives what is directly connected to it.
This example shows how logical analysis is applied to sensory perception.
4
Understand the limitation of perception
Read the second note: 'our perception is not complete, revealing the perceived object as it is in itself.' Perception only captures some inseparable concomitants (lawazim) of the object's specific reality. This is a key epistemological point: the senses provide partial data, not the full essence.
The intellect must then deduce further properties from these concomitants.
5
Recognize the role of the intellect
The author states that the intellect arrives at knowledge of the body's properties by observing the qualities of the reflected ray. This shows that full understanding requires intellectual processing beyond mere sensation. Perception without intellectual attention (e.g., staring absent-mindedly) does not count as true perception.
This ties perception to rationality in Islamic epistemology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأولى: الحواس الخمس: وهي السمع والبصر والذوق واللمس والشم ولا يدرك بها إلا ما اتصل بها إما مباشرة أو بواسطة. فلو قلنا إن المدرك بالبصر هو الجسم، لكان البصر يدرك الجسم بواسطة اتصال الشعاع به، ولكن لو قلنا إن المدرك إنما هو الشعاع المنعكس عن الجسم، فالبصر لا يدرك إلا ما اتصل به، وهو الأصح، ثم إن العقل هو الذي يتوصل إلى معرفة خصائص الجسم من ملاحظة صفات الشعاع المنعكس عنه المتأثر به الدال على بعض خصائصه. هكذا نقول في سائر الحواس.
(2) ينبغى أن يُلاحظ أنه سواء كان الإدراك بالمباشرة كما فى اللمس أو بواسطة كما في الرؤية فلا يكون إدراكنا تاماً كاشفاً عن المُدرَك على هو عليه في نفس الأمر، وإنما يكون إدراكنـا لـبعض لـوازم حقيقتـه المتشخّصة فحسب. والإدراك هو تمثل حقيقة للشيء عند المدرك. وهو إحساس وتخيّل وتوهم وتعقل وسنتكلم عن كل واحد في محله إن شاء الله تعالى. والإدراك الحادث لا بد له عادة من آلة. وليست الحواس الظاهرة سوى نوافذ توصل للنفس صوراً حسية من العالم الخارجى. فهى وسيلة اتصال النفس الوحيــدة مـع = الموجودات الخارجيّة. لذلك قلنا إن الحس شرط عادى فى الإدراك والتعقل والإحساس: إدراك النفس للشيء مكتنفاً ببعض عوارضه ولواحقه المادية، وشرطه كما أشار إليه الشارح حضـور المحسوس الذي لا يكون إلا مادياً، ونسبة خاصة بينه وبين المدرک. فافهم ذلك جيداً.
(3) العلم هنا بالمعنى المصدرى لا الاسمى. وعطف الإدراك على العلم إشارة إلى أنهما عند المنطقيين متساويان. ثم إنه لا إدراك للنفس إلا من حيث ما هى عاقلة، وإليه نبه الشارح المحقق بقوله آنفاً (ثم إن العقل هو الذى يتوصل إلى معرفة خصائص الجسم.. إلخ)، لأنك لو وقفت فاتحاً عینیک شارد العقل لا يقال إنك مدرك لما
The first: the five senses: hearing, sight, taste, touch, and smell. Nothing is perceived by them except what is connected to them, either directly or indirectly. If we say that what is perceived by sight is the body, then sight perceives the body via the connection of the ray to it. But if we say that what is perceived is only the ray reflected from the body, then sight perceives only what is connected to it, and this is more correct. Then the intellect is what arrives at knowledge of the body's properties from observing the qualities of the reflected ray affected by it, indicating some of its properties. Similarly we say for the rest of the senses. (2) It should be noted that whether perception is direct as in touch or indirect as in vision, our perception is not complete, revealing the perceived object as it is in itself. Rather, our perception is only of some of the inseparable concomitants of its specific reality. Perception is the representation of the reality of a thing for the perceiver. It is sensation, imagination, estimation, and intellection, and we will speak about each in its place, God willing. Incident perception usually requires an instrument. The external senses are nothing but windows that convey sensory images to the soul from the external world. So they are the means of connection of the single soul with external existents. Therefore we say that sense is a normal condition for perception, intellection, and sensation: the soul's perception of a thing surrounded by some of its material accidents and attachments. Its condition, as the commentator indicated, is the presence of the sense-object, which cannot be but material, and a special relation between it and the perceiver. Understand that well. (3) Here 'ilm (science) is in the infinitive sense, not the nominal. The conjunction of idrak (perception) with 'ilm indicates that they are equivalent among logicians. Then there is no perception of the soul except insofar as it is rational. The verifying commentator indicated this by his earlier statement (then the intellect is what arrives at knowledge of the body's properties...), because if you stand with your eyes open, mind absent, it is not said that you perceive what...
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage defines the five senses and discusses the nature of perception. The author lists the senses and explains that they only perceive what is connected to them, directly or indirectly. He uses the example of vision: either it perceives the body itself via a ray, or it perceives the reflected ray. The latter is considered more correct. The intellect then deduces the body's properties from the ray's qualities. Note (2) emphasizes that perception is never complete; it only grasps some concomitants of the object's reality. Perception is defined as a representation of the thing, and it encompasses sensation, imagination, estimation, and intellection. The senses are merely windows for the soul. The condition for perception is the presence of a material sense-object and a special relation. Note (3) clarifies that 'ilm and idrak are synonymous for logicians, and perception requires the intellect's attention—without it, even with open eyes, one does not truly perceive.

Key Terms
الحواس الخمس
الإدراك
المباشرة
الواسطة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the view that sight perceives the reflected ray (shu'a') considered more correct than the view that sight perceives the body itself?
A) Because the body is too large to be perceived directly.
B) Because the ray is directly connected to the eye, whereas the body is not.
C) Because the ray contains more information about the body.
D) Because the intellect cannot deduce properties from the body directly.

Key Takeaway
Perception through the senses is always partial and indirect; true understanding requires the active engagement of the intellect.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Consider the debate in Kalam about the beatific vision (ru'ya) in the afterlife. Using the principle from this passage that sight only perceives what is directly connected to it (via a ray), explain why some theologians argued that God cannot be seen physically even in paradise, since God is not material and cannot be connected to the eye.
?
Take an example from Fiqh: the determination of the direction of the Qibla. A jurist uses sensory evidence (stars, compass) but must intellectually deduce the correct direction. Identify which part of the process corresponds to direct perception, indirect perception, and intellectual deduction according to the categories in this passage.

The Intellect: Definition and Nature
Author defines the intellect as a God-given faculty, distinguishing it from substance.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the correct Islamic theological definition of the intellect and distinguish it from the philosophical view that it is a substance.

Core Idea
The intellect is a God-given faculty, not a substance—a key theological distinction.

In this passage, the author defines the intellect (al-'aql) as a faculty deposited by God in humans, serving as an instrument of knowledge. He explicitly refutes the notion that the intellect is a self-subsistent substance, clarifying the position of the mutakallimun. Understanding this definition is foundational for subsequent discussions of knowledge and reasoning in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition
Find the sentence where the author says 'By intellect we mean that faculty...'. This is the core definition.
2
Identify the genus
What broader category does the author place the intellect in? It is called a 'malaka' (faculty) — note this is the genus.
3
Identify the differentia
What distinguishes this faculty from others? It is deposited by God, and it is an instrument for attaining knowledge. Also, it is not a substance.
The passage explicitly denies that 'aql is a jawhar (substance).
4
Check completeness
Does this definition include all instances of intellect? Does it exclude non-intellects? The definition is a rasm (description) rather than a hadd haqiqi, as it gives properties rather than essential constituents.
The author provides a functional description.
5
Contrast with the philosophical view
Note the shift alert: earlier philosophers considered 'aql a separate substance. The author corrects this attribution to the theologians.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والوسيلة الثانية للعلم والإدراك : العقل
ونعني بالعقل تلك الملكة التي أودعها الله تعالى في الإنسان والتي بواسطتها يمكنه أن يصل إلى العلم والمعرفة، ويشتمل علم المنطق على وصف كلي لآليات العقل، فالعقل آلة للمعرفة، وليس العقل عند علمائنا المتكلمين جوهراً قائماً بذاته، كما توهمه البعض، فنسب ذلك إليهم غالطاً عليهم. وأصول التعقل مشتركة بين الجنس البشري (2) ، وليست هي أموراً اختيارية ومسلمات موضوعة عن إرادة أو اختيار من الإنسان، بل هي ثابتة لأصل ثبوت الوجود الإنساني على حسب ما خلقه الله تعالى عليه.
(1) قوله (أصول التعقل) أى قوانين الإدراك وتعقل الشيء إدراكه مجرداً عن الغواشي الغريبة واللواحق المادية التي لا تلزم ماهيته عن ماهيته، فهو نوع من الإدراك على المصطلح عليه من أن الإدراك أعم من التعقل. فلا عمل للعقل فى الصور الحسيّة قبل أن تجردها النفس من تلك اللواحق وبعد تجردها تسمّى المعقولات على ما فيه. والفكر هو حركة النفس فى المعقولات عن قصد. وأما حركتها في الصور المحسوسة المحفوظة فى النفس بما يفيد إدراكها مكتنفه بتلك اللواحق فتخييل والفرق بينه وبين الحس أن فيه تصرفاً في الصور المحسوسة لا يقدر عليها الحس، وكذا أنه لا يشترط له حضور المادة المحسوسة، ولا النسبة الخاصة المشروطان للإحساس.
(2) الجنس بالمعنى اللغوى بمعنى الضرب من الشيء، كما تقول الإبل جنس من البهائم، والمعنى هنـا أن البشـر جنس من الحيوان. وستعرف عما قريب في هذا الكتاب أن البشر على اصطلاح أهل الفـن نـوع مـن جـنس الحيوان.
(3) أى أن كلّ إنسان فقد غرز الله تعالى فيه نفس قوانين التعقل، ولا يمكن أن يعقل وهـو علـى هـذه الخلقـه والفطرة بغير هذه الآليات والقوانين. وعليه فكل تعقل يحدث للإنسان في هذا العالم فهو بالأسباب العاديـة للتعقل التي أبدعها الله تعالى في جبلته.
(4) ظاهر العبارة أنّ هذا العمل الذي يقوم به العقل يكون تلقائياً دون قصد وإرادة، وعليه فيكون من قسم التعقل الاضطراري. وأما النظر فلا بد له من قصد وإرادة. لا يقال التحليل والتركيب والاستنتاج نظر فكيف يجعلـه حاصلاً بالاضطرار. لأنا أولاً فهمنا عبارته على أن عمل العقل ههنا بلا إرادة لأنها غير مذكورة في كلامه، فلو قدرناها لارتفع الإشكال. وثانياً نعم النظر تحليل وتركيب واستنتاج، ولكن لا يلزم أن يكـون كـل تحليل وتركيب واستنتاج نظراً، لأنه ربما يحصل التعقل الاضطراري على نفس قانون التعقل الكسبى ولكن لا تكـــون هذه الخطوات مشعورة. ولقائل أن يقول: هذا يقتضى نفى العلم البديهى المعنى به عندكم أنه ما لا يحتاج فــي
And the second means of knowledge and perception: the intellect. By intellect we mean that faculty which God Almighty has deposited in man, through which he can attain knowledge and cognition. The science of logic contains a comprehensive description of the mechanisms of the intellect. So the intellect is an instrument of knowledge. According to our theologians (mutakallimun), the intellect is not a substance existing by itself, as some have imagined, attributing that to them falsely. The principles of intellection are common to the human species (2), and they are not voluntary matters or postulates placed by will or choice of man. Rather, they are fixed by the essence of human existence according to how God created him. (1) His statement (the principles of intellection) means the laws of perception. Intellection of a thing is its perception stripped of foreign attachments and material attachments that do not follow from its essence. So it is a type of perception according to the terminology that perception is more general than intellection. The intellect has no work in sensory images before the soul strips them of those attachments, and after stripping they are called intelligibles. Thinking (fikr) is the soul's movement among the intelligibles intentionally. As for its movement in the sensory images preserved in the soul, which gives their perception surrounded by those attachments, that is imagination (takhayyul). The difference between it and sense is that it involves manipulation of sensory images that sense cannot do, and also it does not require the presence of the sense-object or the special relation required for sensation. (2) jins (genus) in the lexical sense means a kind of thing, as you say 'camels are a genus of beasts'. The meaning here is that humans are a genus of animal. You will soon learn in this book that humans, in technical terminology, are a species of the genus animal. (3) That is, every human has God implanted the same laws of intellection, and he cannot reason while he is in this creation and nature without these mechanisms and laws. Therefore, every intellection that occurs for a human in this world is through the normal causes of intellection that God created in his constitution. (4) The apparent meaning of the statement is that this work that the intellect does is spontaneous without intention and will, so it falls under involuntary intellection. As for reflection (nazar), it requires intention and will. One cannot say: analysis, composition, and deduction are reflection, so how does it occur involuntarily? First we understood his statement that the intellect's work here is without will because it is not mentioned in his words. If we were to assume will, the problem would be resolved. Second, yes reflection is analysis, composition, and deduction, but it does not follow that every analysis, composition, and deduction is reflection, because involuntary intellection may occur according to the same law of acquired intellection but these steps are not felt. Someone might say: this implies the denial of self-evident knowledge, which according to you is that which does not need...
Source pages p. 14

Commentary
This passage defines the intellect and explains its nature. The author states that the intellect is a faculty given by God, and logic describes its mechanisms. Crucially, the intellect is not a substance (as some philosophers might claim); the theologians (mutakallimun) affirm it is an accident. The principles of intellection are universal and innate, not chosen. Note (1) expands: intellection is perception stripped of material attachments. The soul strips sensory images to produce intelligibles. Thinking (fikr) is intentional movement among intelligibles, while imagination (takhayyul) involves sensory images. Note (2) clarifies 'genus' in a lexical and technical sense. Note (3) emphasizes that the laws of intellection are innate, making all intellection occur through normal, God-given means. Note (4) addresses a potential objection: the intellect's spontaneous operations (analysis, synthesis, deduction) seem like reflection (nazar) but are involuntary. The author argues that such operations can occur without intention, and not all analysis is deliberate reflection. This preserves the category of self-evident (badihi) knowledge, though the note cuts off.

The Operations of the Intellect: Intellection, Thinking, and Imagination
Author explains the operations of the intellect: intellection, thinking, imagination, reflection.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between intellection (ta'aqqul), thinking (fikr), imagination (takhayyul), and reflection (nazar) based on their objects and whether they are deliberate or spontaneous.

Core Idea
Intellection strips away material attachments; thinking is deliberate; imagination works with sensory images; reflection requires will.

After defining the intellect, the passage and its commentary describe how the intellect operates. There is a hierarchy: perception is general, intellection is a specific type of perception. Thinking (fikr) is intentional movement among intelligibles, while imagination (takhayyul) manipulates sensory images without needing the sensed object. Reflection (nazar) is deliberate and voluntary. This lesson helps you map these mental acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overarching category
The passage says 'perception is more general than intellection.' Note that idrak is the broad category encompassing all mental awareness.
2
Define intellection (ta'aqqul)
Intellection is perception stripped of foreign and material attachments that are not essential to the thing's essence. It produces intelligibles.
The soul strips sensory images to produce intelligibles.
3
Distinguish thinking (fikr) from imagination (takhayyul)
Fikr is the soul's intentional movement among intelligibles. Takhayyul is movement among sensory images preserved in the soul, without requiring the sensed object's presence or a special relation. Imagination can manipulate images in ways sense cannot.
Fikr is deliberate, takhayyul may be spontaneous.
4
Understand reflection (nazar)
Nazar is deliberate, intentional movement of the intellect in intelligibles, requiring will and choice. It is contrasted with spontaneous intellection.
Note (4) argues that some intellectual operations like analysis can occur involuntarily, so not all analysis is nazar.
5
Apply the distinctions
Given an example of a mental act, classify it as ta'aqqul, fikr, takhayyul, or nazar based on whether it involves intelligibles or sensory images, and whether it is deliberate.

Definition of Indication and Division of Signifier
Definition of indication and division of signifier into verbal and non-verbal.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define indication (dalala) as per the logicians and distinguish between verbal and non-verbal signifiers.

Core Idea
Indication is potential understanding, not actual understanding.

Logicians begin with words because they are the primary vehicle for meanings. They define indication as a property where one thing can potentially convey another. This definition avoids the problem of requiring actual understanding. They then divide signifiers into verbal and non-verbal types.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definition of indication
Find in the Arabic the phrase 'كون أمر بحيث يفهم منه أمر آخر'. Note that it defines indication as a state of a thing from which another thing can be understood.
The definition emphasizes potentiality, not actuality.
2
Examine the condition of potential understanding
The commentator explicitly states that actual understanding is not required; only possibility matters. Why is this important? Because if actual understanding were required, then a signifier would cease to be a signifier when not understood.
3
Understand the division of signifier
The signifier (dal) is divided into verbal (lafzi) and non-verbal (ghayr lafzi). Think of examples: smoke for fire (non-verbal), the word 'fire' (verbal).
Non-verbal includes natural signs and conventional signs.
4
Relate to the purpose of logic
This definition and division regulate the relationship between words and meanings, enabling precise expression in Islamic sciences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أقول: إن علم المنطق لا يتعلق بالألفاظ، كما أوضحناه سابقاً، بل هو يتعلق بالمعاني، وبكيفية الوصول إليهـا من حيث هي علوم ومطلوبات ولكن ما دامت الطريقة الأشهر بين البشر في توصيل المعاني المكتسبة والعلوم المستحصلة هي اللغات المتكونة من الألفاظ والكلمات ، فإن علماء المنطق وضعوا مقدمة في كتب المنطق يبينون فيها العلاقة بين الألفاظ والمعاني من حيث الدلالة، وذلك لأن الألفاظ مجرد دلالات على المعاني وليست مولدة لها أصالة، فلذلك بحث العلماء في الألفاظ من هذه الحيثية. والهدف من بحثهم هذا هو ضبط العلاقة الدلالية بين الألفاظ والمعاني بحيث يتم التعبير بالشكل المطلوب والمطابق على ما يريدون بيانه.
تعريف الدلالة وأقسامها:
(2)..
الدلالة بحسب تعريف المناطقة: كونُ أمر بحيث يفهم منه أمر آخر (3). وهذا التعريف لا يشترط لتحقق الدلالة أن يفهم الأمر الثاني بالفعل من الأول، ولكن يشترط إمكانية الفهم ، فلو لم يفهم لما انتفى كون الأول دالاً، والثاني مدلولا (4).
والدال ينقسم إلى لفظ وإلى غير لفظ.
أى التصور، وتقرأ فعل أمر فنصب، أو ماض مبنى للمعلوم فنصب، أو ماض مبني للمجهول فرفع. والأول أليقها بناصح للمبتدى والنظرى والضروري قسما العلم على ما بينهما الشارح. والله تعالى أعلم.
(1) قوله (المتكونة من الألفاظ لأن اللغة أعم من أن تكون بالألفاظ وكذا الكلام على ما تقرر في محلّه. (2) يقال دل دلالة ودلالة ودلوله، وهى بفتح الدال أعلى. والدلالة قيل: هي فهم أمر من أمر. واعترض بأن الدلالة وصف للدال والفهم وصف للفاهم، فيلزم على هذا التعريف تفسير ما هو وصف لشيء بما هو وصف لغيــره. وأجيب عنه بجواب حسن. فاختار الشارح تعريفاً آخر كي لا يرد عليه هذا السؤال. (3) قوله (كون أمر .. ( أى بحالة بحيث يلزم من العلم به العلم بأمر آخر.
(4) أى فى نفس الأمر. فالدليل دليل فى نفسه سواء عرفناه أو لا. فهو دالّ بالقوة على مدلوله ما دام دليلاً. انک لو دلک احمرار وجه أخيك على خجله، فإن احمرار وجهه يسمى دالاً، وخجله مدلولاً، والنسبة بينهما دلالة.
I say: The science of logic is not concerned with words, as we have clarified previously, but rather with meanings, and with the manner of reaching them insofar as they are sciences and objects of inquiry. However, since the most famous method among humans for conveying acquired meanings and obtained sciences is languages composed of words and expressions, the logicians placed an introduction in their logic books explaining the relationship between words and meanings in terms of indication. This is because words are merely indicators of meanings and are not originally generative of them. Therefore scholars examined words from this aspect. The goal of their examination is to regulate the semantic relationship between words and meanings so that expression occurs in the required and corresponding form to what they intend to explain.
Definition of indication and its divisions:
(2)
Indication, according to the definition of the logicians, is: a thing being such that another thing is understood from it (3). This definition does not require for the realization of indication that the second thing is actually understood from the first, but it requires the possibility of understanding. So if it is not understood, that does not negate that the first is a signifier and the second is signified (4).
The signifier is divided into verbal and non-verbal.
[Matn:]
أنواع الدلالة الوضعية
دلالة اللفظ على ما وافقه
يدعونه دلالة المطابقة
وجزئه تضمنا وما لزم فالتزام إن بعقل التزم
[End of matn]
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a definitional introduction to the topic of indication (dalala) in logic. The commentator first justifies why logicians study words despite logic being about meanings: because words are the primary vehicle for conveying meanings. He then defines indication: a thing (the signifier) being such that another thing (the signified) is understood from it. Importantly, the definition requires only the potential for understanding, not actual understanding. The signifier is then divided into verbal (lafzi) and non-verbal (ghayr lafzi). Following this, the commentator introduces the matn on the types of conventional indication (dalala wad'iyya): a word indicates its agreed-upon meaning by correspondence (mutabaqa), indicates a part of that meaning by inclusion (tadammun), and indicates an implied meaning by implication (iltizam), provided it is mentally accompanied. The commentator's own text includes a discussion of the definition and a note about the etymology of the word dalala. The commentary explains that the chosen definition avoids the objection that 'understanding' is a property of the person, not the signifier.

Key Terms
دلالة
دال
مدلول
لفظ
غير لفظ

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The actual understanding of a meaning from a word.
B) A thing being such that another thing is understood from it, requiring potential understanding.
C) The relationship between a word and its meaning.
D) The process of deriving meanings from words.

Key Takeaway
Indication is the potential of a signifier to convey a signified, not the act of being understood.

Three Types of Conventional Verbal Indication
Matn listing the three types of conventional verbal indication.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a word indicates its full meaning (mutabaqa), a part of it (tadammun), or an implied meaning (iltizam) in a given example.

Core Idea
A word can indicate its whole meaning, a part, or an accompanying idea.

The matn presents the three ways a conventional word can indicate its meaning: correspondence (mutabaqa) for the entire assigned meaning, inclusion (tadammun) for a part, and implication (iltizam) for a necessary mental accompaniment. This classification helps in analyzing definitions and interpreting texts.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the three Arabic terms
مطابقة (mutabaqa), تضمن (tadammun), التزام (iltizam). Understand their literal meanings: correspondence, inclusion, implication.
2
Understand each type with examples
For 'house': mutabaqa indicates the whole building; tadammun indicates a part like a room; iltizam indicates something necessarily implied like a roof.
Iltizam requires the accompaniment to be mental (bi 'aql), not arbitrary.
3
Apply to Islamic vocabulary
Consider the word 'الصلاة' (prayer): mutabaqa indicates the entire act; tadammun indicates a part like ركوع (bowing); iltizam indicates the implied meaning of devotion.
4
Distinguish tadammun from iltizam
Tadammun is a part of the definition; iltizam is not part but necessarily associated. Knowing the difference prevents confusion in arguments.

I say: The science of logic is not concerned with words, as we have clarified previously, but rather with meanings, and with the manner of reaching them insofar as they are sciences and objects of inquiry. However, since the most famous method among humans for conveying acquired meanings and obtained sciences is languages composed of words and expressions, the logicians placed an introduction in their logic books explaining the relationship between words and meanings in terms of indication. This is because words are merely indicators of meanings and are not originally generative of them. Therefore scholars examined words from this aspect. The goal of their examination is to regulate the semantic relationship between words and meanings so that expression occurs in the required and corresponding form to what they intend to explain.
Definition of indication and its divisions:
(2)
Indication, according to the definition of the logicians, is: a thing being such that another thing is understood from it (3). This definition does not require for the realization of indication that the second thing is actually understood from the first, but it requires the possibility of understanding. So if it is not understood, that does not negate that the first is a signifier and the second is signified (4).
The signifier is divided into verbal and non-verbal.
[Matn:]
أنواع الدلالة الوضعية
دلالة اللفظ على ما وافقه
يدعونه دلالة المطابقة
وجزئه تضمنا وما لزم فالتزام إن بعقل التزم
[End of matn]
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a definitional introduction to the topic of indication (dalala) in logic. The commentator first justifies why logicians study words despite logic being about meanings: because words are the primary vehicle for conveying meanings. He then defines indication: a thing (the signifier) being such that another thing (the signified) is understood from it. Importantly, the definition requires only the potential for understanding, not actual understanding. The signifier is then divided into verbal (lafzi) and non-verbal (ghayr lafzi). Following this, the commentator introduces the matn on the types of conventional indication (dalala wad'iyya): a word indicates its agreed-upon meaning by correspondence (mutabaqa), indicates a part of that meaning by inclusion (tadammun), and indicates an implied meaning by implication (iltizam), provided it is mentally accompanied. The commentator's own text includes a discussion of the definition and a note about the etymology of the word dalala. The commentary explains that the chosen definition avoids the objection that 'understanding' is a property of the person, not the signifier.

التزام

The Three Types of Verbal Conventional Connotation
Defines and classifies the three types of verbal conventional connotation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of verbal conventional connotation (dalala wad'iyya) and correctly categorize examples from Arabic texts.

Core Idea
A word can signify its full meaning, a part of it, or a necessary concomitant—know which is which.

In logic, words are mere indicators of meanings, but they can indicate in three distinct ways: by corresponding to the entire meaning, by containing a part, or by implying something necessarily connected. This lesson unpacks these three forms of connotation using examples from the Islamic intellectual tradition.

Guided Path
1
Grasp the definition of dalala
Connotation (الدلالة) is defined as 'a thing being such that another thing is understood from it.' Note that actual understanding is not required; possibility suffices.
2
Identify the three types from the matn
The matn states: al-mutabaqa for the whole meaning, al-tadammun for a part, and al-iltizam for a necessary concomitant. Commit this classification to memory.
The order is correspondence, containment, implication.
3
Apply the types to commentary examples
The commentary gives examples: 'lion' for the animal is mutabaqa; for its tail is tadammun; for ferocity is iltizam. Do the same for 'date' and 'human'.
4
Test with a new Islamic term
Take the word 'شهادة' (shahada). Does it indicate the full statement of faith (mutabaqa), a part like the utterance (tadammun), or a necessary effect like salvation (iltizam)? Justify your answer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال: [أنواع الدلالةِ الوَضْعِيَّة ] دَلالَةُ اللَّفْظِ عَلى ما وافَقَهُ يَدْعُونَهَا دَلالَةَ المُطابَقَة وَجُزْئِهِ تَضَمُّنَا وَمَا لَزِمْ فَهْوَ الْتِزام إِنْ بِعَقْلِ الْتَزَمْ
أقول: إن علم المنطق لا يتعلق بالألفاظ، كما أوضحناه سابقاً، بل هو يتعلق بالمعاني، وبكيفية الوصول إليهـا من حيث هي علوم ومطلوبات ولكن ما دامت الطريقة الأشهر بين البشر في توصيل المعاني المكتسبة والعلوم المستحصلة هي اللغات المتكونة من الألفاظ والكلمات، فإن علماء المنطق وضعوا مقدمة في كتب المنطق يبينون فيها العلاقة بين الألفاظ والمعاني من حيث الدلالة، وذلك لأن الألفاظ مجرد دلالات على المعاني وليست مولدة لها أصالة، فلذلك بحث العلماء في الألفاظ من هذه الحيثية. والهدف من بحثهم هذا هو ضبط العلاقة الدلالية بين الألفاظ والمعاني بحيث يتم التعبير بالشكل المطلوب والمطابق على ما يريدون بيانه.
تعريف الدلالة وأقسامها:
الدلالة بحسب تعريف المناطقة: كونُ أمر بحيث يفهم منه أمر آخر. وهذا التعريف لا يشترط لتحقق الدلالة أن يفهم الأمر الثاني بالفعل من الأول، ولكن يشترط إمكانية الفهم، فلو لم يفهم لما انتفى كون الأول دالاً، والثاني مدلولا.
والدال ينقسم إلى لفظ وإلى غير لفظ.
فغير اللفظ إما دال بالعقل كدلالة التغير على الحدوث، أو بالعادة كدلالة المطر على النبات والحمرة على الخجل والصفرة على الوجل، أو بالوضع كدلالة الإشارة باليد أو الرأس مثلاً على معنى "نعم" أو "لا".
واللفظ إما دال بالعقل كدلالة اللفظ على وجود اللافظ من وراء جدار، أو بالعادة كدلالة أخ " على وجع الصدر، أو بالوضع كدلالة لفظ أسد على الحيوان المفترس، وهذه الدلالة الوضعية هي المعتبرة في المنطق، فلا يعتبر شيء من الدلالات الأخرى عند المناطقة.
والدلالة الثابتة بين اللفظ وبين المعنى هي دلالة وضعية، بمعنى أنها ليست دلالة عقلية، ولا دلالة عادية، بل وضعية، ومعنى الوضع هنا هو أن إرادة عاقل مختار خصصت كل لفظ بما يدل عليه. وعقلنا في هذه الحالة، ينتقل بين اللفظ والمعنى، فالعقل عندما يحضر عنده اللفظ، إما أن يستحضر نفس المعنى الذي وضع اللفظ دالاً عليه، أو أن يستحضر لازم المعنى الموضوع عليه اللفظ، وقد ينتقل إلى جزء من هذا المعنى. فالدلالة الأولى تسمى دلالة مطابقة، والثانية تسمى دلالة الملازمة، والثالثة تسمى تضمنية. فدلالة اللفظ على المعنى الموضوع له بتمامه تسمى دلالة مطابقة. ومثالها دلالة كلمة "أسد" على الحيوان المفترس المعروف، ودلالة كلمة التمر على الفاكهة المعروفة. ودلالة الإنسان على "الحيوان الناطق". وأما دلالة اللفظ على جزء معناه فإنها تسمى دلالة تَضَمُّن، لأن المعنى المدلول عليه متضمن في المعنى الموضوع له اللفظ مطابقة. كدلالة الأسد على ذنبه، والتمر على طعمه أو شكله. والمنزل على الباب.
He said: [Types of conventional connotation] The connotation of a word for what corresponds to it they call connotation of correspondence, and for its part they call connotation of containment, and whatever is necessary [by the mind] is connotation of implication if it is necessitated by the mind. I say: The science of logic does not pertain to words, as we clarified earlier, but rather pertains to meanings and the manner of attaining them insofar as they are knowledge and objects of inquiry. However, since the most common method among humans for conveying acquired meanings and obtained sciences is languages composed of words and expressions, the logicians placed an introduction in logic books in which they explain the relationship between words and meanings in terms of connotation, because words are merely indicators of meanings and are not original generators of them. Therefore, scholars investigated words from this perspective. The goal of this investigation is to regulate the semantic relationship between words and meanings so that expression occurs in the desired and corresponding form for what they intend to explain. Definition of connotation and its divisions: Connotation according to the definition of the logicians is: a thing being such that another thing is understood from it. This definition does not require that the second thing be actually understood from the first, but rather requires the possibility of understanding; if it is not understood, it does not negate that the first is a signifier and the second is a signified. The signifier is divided into verbal and non-verbal. Non-verbal is either rational, like the connotation of change for origination; or customary, like the connotation of rain for plants, redness for shyness, and yellowness for fear; or conventional, like the connotation of pointing with the hand or head, for example, to the meaning of "yes" or "no". Verbal is either rational, like the connotation of a word for the existence of the speaker from behind a wall; or customary, like the connotation of "brother" for chest pain; or conventional, like the connotation of the word "lion" for the predatory animal. This conventional connotation is the one considered in logic; none of the other connotations are considered by the logicians. The connotation established between a word and its meaning is a conventional connotation, meaning it is not rational nor customary, but conventional. The meaning of convention here is that the will of a free, rational agent has specified each word to indicate what it indicates. In this case, our mind moves between the word and the meaning. When the word is present to the mind, it either evokes the very meaning for which the word was coined, or it evokes a necessary concomitant of the meaning for which the word was coined, or it moves to a part of this meaning. The first connotation is called connotation of correspondence, the second is called connotation of implication (necessary concomitance), and the third is called connotation of containment. So the connotation of a word for the complete meaning for which it was coined is called connotation of correspondence. Its example is the connotation of the word "lion" for the well-known predatory animal, and the connotation of the word "date" for the well-known fruit, and the connotation of "human" for "rational animal". As for the connotation of a word for a part of its meaning, it is called connotation of containment, because the signified meaning is contained within the meaning for which the word was coined by correspondence, such as the connotation of "lion" for its tail, and "date" for its taste or shape, and "house" for the door.
Source pages p. 23

Commentary
This passage is a definitional and classificatory exposition of the types of verbal conventional connotation (al-dalala al-lafziyya al-wad'iyya). The author begins by citing the matn (poem) from al-Sullam, which states the three types: مطابقة (correspondence) for the word signifying its full meaning, تضمن (containment) for a part of that meaning, and التزام (implication) for a necessary concomitant. Then the commentary expands on this. The author first justifies why logic must discuss words: although logic deals with meanings, the most common medium for conveying meanings is language, so logicians include an introduction on the relation between words and meanings. Then he defines dalala (connotation) as a thing being such that another thing is understood from it, noting that actual understanding is not required—only the possibility. He then divides the signifier into verbal and non-verbal. For non-verbal, he gives examples of rational (change indicating origination), customary (rain indicating plants, redness indicating shyness), and conventional (pointing indicating 'yes' or 'no'). For verbal, similarly: rational (a voice indicating a speaker behind a wall), customary ('brother' indicating chest pain), and conventional (the word 'lion' indicating the animal). He stresses that only the verbal conventional connotation is considered in logic. He then explains the nature of conventional connotation: it is established by the will of a rational agent who assigns each word to a meaning. The mind, upon hearing a word, can grasp either the full meaning (مطابقة), a part of it (تضمن), or a necessary concomitant (التزام). The commentary slightly misorders the second and third names in one sentence (calling the second 'الملازمة' and third 'تضمنية'), but the matn and the subsequent examples clarify the correct order: مطابقة for the whole, تضمن for a part, التزام for a necessary implication. Examples: 'lion' corresponds to the animal (مطابقة), 'lion' indicates its tail by containment (تضمن), and presumably 'lion' indicates ferocity by implication (التزام). The author gives examples for مطابقة and تضمن, but the text cuts off before discussing التزام in detail. The passage thus establishes the foundational semantic framework for logical analysis of terms.

دلالة المطابقة
دلالة التضمن
دلالة الالتزام
الوضع

Understanding Dalalat al-Iltizam – Definition and Conditions
Author defines iltizam and discusses its conditions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given example constitutes valid indication by entailment (dalalat al-iltizam) based on the conditions of mental necessity and intellectual observation.

Core Idea
Iltizam requires a necessary mental connection, not just frequent external correlation.

In this passage, the author defines dalalat al-iltizam and distinguishes it from other types of indication. The key condition is that the mental transition must be by intellectual observation, not merely by habit or custom. This lesson will help you apply this condition to evaluate examples from Islamic theology and logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Locate the term being defined in the Arabic: دلالة الالتزام. It is a type of indication where the word points to a meaning that necessarily accompanies its original meaning.
2
Understand the definition
The definition: indication of a word on a meaning that is a necessary concomitant (lāzim) of its originally posited meaning. The mind moves from the direct meaning to the concomitant by intellectual observation.
Example: 'four' indicates evenness, as the mind necessarily associates the number four with being even.
3
Analyze the condition
The condition: the transition must be by mental observation (bi-mulāḥaẓat al-ʿaql), not by custom or mere word association. The raven example (blackness) fails because the connection is only external—one can imagine a white raven.
The theological example of ḥudūth (origination) necessitating qidam (eternity) is valid because it's a mental necessity.
4
Test examples
Apply the condition to the examples: 'four' and evenness (valid if four is defined as 'a number having two pairs'), 'blindness' and sight (valid because blindness is defined as absence of sight, necessitating sight in the mind).
The marginal note clarifies the example of four depends on the definition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لاحتوائه عليه. ويلاحظ في هذه الدلالة أن العقل ينتقل فيها من ملاحظة الكل إلى الجزء. ففيها حركة عقلية ما.
(1)..
(2)
وأما دلالة اللفظ على معنى لازم لمعناه الموضوع له مطابقة، فإنها تسمى دلالة التزام، كما تدل الأربعة على الزوجية، وكدلالة العمى على البصر ، لأن العمى هو عدم البصر، فإن استحضر الذهن مفهوم العمى وهو المدلول المطابقى لكلمة العمى، فإن الذهن ينتقل إلى مفهوم البصر مباشرة. ويشترط في دلالة الالتزام أن يكون الانتقال بملاحظة العقل لا بمجرد اللفظ ) أو العادة، فانتقال العقل من المعنى المطابقي إلى معنى لازم عنه عند العقل، فالعقل عندما يتصور معنى الحدوث ينتقل إلى معنى القدم، حتى لو لم يتبادر إلى الإنسان لفظ القدم، ولذلك فإنه عندما يسمع لفظ الحدوث، يفهم مطابقة معنى الحدوث، وينتقل عقله إلى معنى القدم مباشرة. ولا يشترط في التلازم العقلي أن يكون بين المعنيين تلازم في الخارج أيضاً، بل الأمر في ذلك سواء، أي لو كان تلازم خارجي أيضاً بينها، أو لم يكن فلا إشكال. فمثال ما بينهما تلازم عند الذهن وفي الخارج الزوجية للأربعة، ومثال ما بينهما تلازم في الخارج ولكن لا تتحقق الملازمة في الذهن السواد للغراب، فكل غراب في الخارج فهو أسود، ولكن لا يوجد تلازم عقلي للغراب مع السواد لأنه يمكن توهم غراب أبيض.
بتوسط الوضع، والوضع إنما يكون على المعنى الذهنى أو المعنى مطلقاً لا بقيد الذهن أو الخارج، وكونـه علـى المتشخص في الخارج مذهب فاسد كما قرره الشارح الفاضل في بعض مقالاته. ثم إنهم يصرحون بانحصار دلالــه المطابقة والتضمن، وبرفضهم التوسع فى دلالة الالتزام لأنها تفضى إلى مدلولات لا حصر لها، فإذا اعتبرنا التشخص الخارجي في التضمن فإنه يفضي إلى عدم انضباط هذه الدلالة من نفس الباب، لأنه سيفضي بنا إلى جعل اللفظ دالاً على كل جزء من أجزاء اء مصداقه المتشخص، فلا تنضبط هذه الدلالة لكثرة أجزائه وخفاء بعضها. كما أن دلالة اللفظ علـى جزء المصداق قد تشتبه بدلالة الالتزام الخارجى وكذلك فإن قسمة الدلالات بحسب المدلول تامة، وهو إمـا الــداخل في الماهية أو الخارج عنها، فإن كان داخلاً فهو إما الكل أو الجزء الأل المطابقة والثانى التضمن. وإن كان خارجاً عنها لازما لها فالتزام واعتبار التشخص الخارجي في التضمن قد يجعلها خارجة عن الذات وجزءاً منها في آن. والمدلول الخارج عن الذات لا بد أن يكون لازماً للذات لزوماً بيناً، وإلا لم يصح كونه مدلولاً لعنوانها، واعتبار التشخص فــي التضمنية على هذا يستدعى كون المدلول لازماً للذات ذهناً وخارجاً، وفيه نقض للقسمة. هذا وإن مناقشة الأمثلة ليست من دأب الفحول والمثال لا يعدو أن يكون وسيلة لتقريب المفهوم، فما دام كلام الشارح صحيحاً في توضيحه، فلا يضر علمه وتحقيقه ما ساقه لتقريب الصورة للمبتدى بمثال فيه ما نبهنا عليه.
(1) اعلم أنه لا يتم كون لفظ أربعة دالاً على الزوجية بالالتزام لزوماً بيناً بالمعنى الأخص في الذهن والخارج كمـا سيمثل به، إلا إذا جعلت معنى الأربعة المطابقي هو عدد ذا الزوجين. وعندها فمجرد ذكر الأربعة يستدعى معناهـا المخصوص هذا أى العدد ذا الزوجين، فكما ترى كان مجرد تصور الأربعة بهذا المعنى مستدعياً لمعنى الزوجيــه خارجاً وذهناً.
(2) أى كما هي الحال فى دلالة المطابقة . فبمجرد ذكر اللفظ يحضر المعنى.
Because it contains it. And it is observed in this indication that the mind moves from observing the whole to the part. So there is a certain mental movement. (1).. (2) As for the indication of a word on a meaning necessary to its originally posited meaning by correspondence, it is called indication by entailment, as 'four' indicates evenness, and as 'blindness' indicates sight, because blindness is the absence of sight. When the mind conceives the meaning of blindness—which is the correlated meaning of the word blindness—the mind then moves immediately to the meaning of sight. It is required in indication by entailment that the transition be by mental observation, not merely by the word or custom. So the mind moves from the correlated meaning to a meaning necessary to it in the mind. For when the mind conceives the meaning of origination (ḥudūth), it moves to the meaning of eternity (qidam), even if the word 'eternity' does not occur to the person. Therefore, when he hears the word 'origination', he understands by correspondence the meaning of origination, and his mind moves directly to the meaning of eternity. And it is not a condition in mental entailment that there be a correlation between the two meanings in the external world as well. Rather, the matter is the same in that regard: whether there is also an external correlation between them or not, there is no problem. An example of what has a correlation in the mind and externally is evenness for four. And an example of what has a correlation externally but the entailment is not actualized in the mind is blackness for the raven: every raven in the external world is black, but there is no mental entailment for the raven with blackness because a white raven can be imagined. By the act of positing (waḍʿ), and positing is only on the mental meaning or meaning absolutely without restriction to mind or external world, and its being on the particular in the external world is a corrupt doctrine as the excellent commentator has established in some of his articles. Then they declare that the indications of correspondence and inclusion are limited, and they reject expansion in indication by entailment because it leads to countless significations. For if we consider external particularity in inclusion, it leads to the lack of regulation of this indication from the same perspective, because it would lead us to making the word indicate every part of the parts of its particular instantiation, so this indication would not be regulated due to the multiplicity of its parts and the obscurity of some of them. Also, the indication of the word on a part of the instantiation may be confused with indication by external entailment. And likewise, the division of indications according to the signified is complete: it is either inside the essence or outside it. If it is inside, it is either the whole or the part: the first is correspondence, the second is inclusion. If it is outside it as a necessary concomitant, it is entailment. And considering external particularity in inclusion may make it both outside the essence and a part of it at the same time. The signified outside the essence must be a necessary concomitant of the essence with a clear necessity, otherwise it would not be valid for it to be signified by its title. And considering particularity in inclusion on this basis requires that the signified be a necessary concomitant of the essence mentally and externally, and that is a violation of the division. This is so, and criticizing examples is not the practice of the eminent scholars; the example is only a means to approximate the concept. As long as the commentator's speech is correct in its clarification, it does not harm his knowledge and investigation what he brings to approximate the picture for the beginner with an example that contains what we have pointed out. (1) Know that the word 'four' does not validly indicate evenness by entailment with a clear necessity in the specific sense in the mind and the external world as will be exemplified, unless the correlated meaning of four is made to be a number having two pairs. In that case, merely mentioning 'four' calls to mind its specific meaning, which is the number having two pairs. As you see, merely conceiving four in this sense necessitates the meaning of evenness externally and mentally. (2) Meaning, as is the case in indication by correspondence: merely mentioning the word brings the meaning to mind.
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage from the Muyassar Sullam commentary defines and explains indication by entailment (dalālat al-iltizām). The text begins by noting that in this type of indication, the mind moves from the whole to the part, indicating a mental operation. It then defines iltizām as a word's indication of a meaning that is necessary to its originally posited meaning, calling it 'indication by entailment.' Examples given are 'four' indicating evenness and 'blindness' indicating sight. The key condition is that the mental transition must be by intellectual observation (bi-mulāḥaẓat al-ʿaql), not merely by the word or custom. This is illustrated with the theological example of ḥudūth (origination) necessitating qidam (eternity) in the mind, even without the word 'qidam' being uttered. The author then clarifies that external correlation is not required; only mental entailment matters. An example of external correlation without mental entailment is the blackness of ravens—here, blackness is externally correlated but not mentally necessary because a white raven can be imagined. The commentary then enters into a deeper discussion about waḍʿ (positing), restricting the types of indication to three (correspondence, inclusion, entailment), and argues against extending inclusion to external particulars, as that would lead to countless significations and violate the division. The author emphasizes that the division based on the signified is exhaustive: either inside the essence (whole or part, i.e., mutābaqa or taḍammun) or outside it as a necessary concomitant (iltizām). Considering external particularity in inclusion would confuse it with entailment. Finally, a marginal note clarifies that the example of 'four' and evenness requires a specific definition of four to be a valid example of iltizām. Throughout, the passage shows careful logical precision in distinguishing the three types of indication.

دلالة الالتزام
ملازمة

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is a valid example of indication by entailment (dalālat al-iltizām)?
A) The word 'raven' indicating blackness because all ravens are black externally.
B) The word 'origination' (ḥudūth) indicating eternity (qidam) in the mind.
C) The word 'human' indicating 'animal' because animal is part of its meaning.
D) The word 'house' indicating 'door' because a door is part of a house.

Key Takeaway
The validity of dalalat al-iltizam depends on a necessary mental connection, not external coincidence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is the indication of 'blindness' on 'sight' a valid iltizam? Explain using the condition of mental observation.
?
Identify whether 'raven' on 'blackness' is iltizam and why.

intermediate
8 min
The Exhaustive Division of Indications and the Rejection of External Particularity
Author discusses the exhaustive division and critiques external particularity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the classical tripartite division of indication is exhaustive and why including external particulars in inclusion is rejected.

Core Idea
Indication is either inside the essence (whole or part) or outside as necessary concomitant – no fourth type.

The passage extends the discussion to the broader classification of indications, arguing that considering external particulars in inclusion leads to endless significations and undermines the division. This lesson will clarify this classification and the commentator's reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Recall the three types
The three types are mutābaqa (correspondence, the whole meaning), taḍammun (inclusion, a part of the meaning), and iltizām (entailment, a necessary concomitant outside the meaning).
2
Understand the division principle
The division is based on the signified's relation to the essence (māhiyya). If the signified is inside the essence, it is either the whole (mutābaqa) or a part (taḍammun). If it is outside the essence but necessary, it is iltizām.
This division is considered exhaustive: no signified can be both inside and outside.
3
Analyze the objection
The commentator rejects considering external particularity (al-tashakhkhuṣ al-khārijī) in taḍammun, because it leads to countless significations (every external part becomes signified) and blurs the line between inside and outside, effectively turning taḍammun into iltizām.
The marginal note clarifies that the example of 'four' indicating evenness only works if 'four' is defined appropriately, reinforcing the need for precision.

Source Text

(1)..

Indication by Correspondence (Dalālat al-Muṭābaqa)
Definition and classification of muṭābaqa with examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a given word-meaning relation is an instance of indication by correspondence (muṭābaqa) and classify it by the type of word and meaning involved.

Core Idea
Correspondence is when a word covers its entire posited meaning.

In this lesson, we explore the first and most direct type of verbal indication: correspondence (muṭābaqa). The author defines it as when a word indicates the complete meaning for which it was coined. Through examples from human to horse and even the Divine Names, you will learn to recognize muṭābaqa in both simple and composite meanings.

Guided Path
1
Understand the division
The author divides verbal indication into two: indicates the entire meaning or not. Muṭābaqa is the case where it indicates the entire meaning.
2
Identify the definition
Note that muṭābaqa requires the word to cover all aspects of its posited meaning, with no part omitted.
3
Explore the examples
Examine the examples given: 'insān' for 'rational animal', 'faras' for 'whinnying animal'. These are single words indicating composite meanings.
4
Note the subtypes
The author lists four combinations: single word to simple meaning, single word to composite meaning, compound expression to simple meaning, compound expression to composite meaning. Check each example.
5
Apply to theological context
Consider how the names of Allah (e.g., 'Allāh') indicate the simple Essence by correspondence, avoiding any composition.

اعلم أن اللفظ الدال بالوضع على معنى معين إما أن يدل على تمام ذلك المعنى، أى يدل على ذلك المعنى بعينه وتمامه بحيث لا يخرج شيء من أجزاء المعنى التي اعتبرها الواضع ولاحظها في مقابلة اللفظ، أو لا يدل على تمام ذلك المعنى. فإذا دل اللفظ على تمام المعنى الموضوع له، سميت الدلالة اللفظية الوضعية دلالة مطابقة. وذلك لتطابق أى توافق اللفظ والمعنى. ومثاله دلالة الإنسان على الحيوان الناطق. والفرس على الحيوان الصهال، إلى غير ذلك. ولاحظ أن دلالة المطابقة قد تكون فى المعنى المركب كما في دلالة الإنسان على الحيوان الناطق فإنه معنى مركب من الحيوانية والناطقية، وقد تكون فى المعنى الذى لا يتصور فيه التركب والتجزؤ، كما نقول لفظ الجوهر الفرد يدل على الجزء الذى لا يتجزأ وهو معنى بسيط غيـر كب، وكذلك حين نطلق أسماء الله سبحانه الحسنى عليه، فإنها دالة على الذات الأقدس واجب الوجوب الغنى المنزه المتعالى عن سمات النقص والحدث من التركب والتبعض ونحوهما مما لا يعقل في القديم. واعلم أيضاً: أن المطابقة واقعة بين اللفظ المفرد والمعنى البسيط، وواقعه بين اللفظ المفرد والمعنى المركب، بين اللفظ المركب والمعنى البسيط، وواقعه بين اللفظ المركب والمعنى المركب. مثال الأول لفظ الجلالة الله على واجب الوجود ومثال الثانى الإنسان على الحيوان الناطق، ومثال الثالث واجب الوجود على الإله، ومثال الرابع لفظ أصول الفقه على طرق الفقه المجملة.
مر
وواقعه
من
وأما إذا لم يكن اللفظ دالاً على تمام المعنى الذى وضع له، فإما أن يدل على جزء المعنى الموضوع لـه، أى بأن يكون المعنى الذى وضع له اللفظ معنى مركباً له جز آن فصاعداً فيدل اللفظ على جزء من أجزاء ذلــك المعنى المركب. أو لا يدل حتى على جزء المعنى الذي وضع اللفظ بإزائه. فإذا كان اللفظ دالاً علـى جـزء المعنى الذي وضع هذا اللفظ له سميت الدلالة دلالة تضمنية، لكون الجزء في ضمن كل المعنى الموضوع لـه. ولاحظ أن الدلالة التضمنية لا يمكن تصورها إلا فى المعانى المركبة أى ذات الأجزاء، بخلاف المطابقية كما بينته لك. وبقى لتمام القسمة، أن يدلّ اللفظ على معنى لا هو تمام المعنى الموضوع له، ولا هو جزؤه، فيلــزم ذلك أن يدل على شيء آخر خارج عن حقيقة المعنى الذى وضع اللفظ بإزائه ولكنه لازم لها، وهذا القسم الدلالة هو ما يسمونه دلالة الالتزام. ولا بد فيها من علاقة تلازمية بين المعنى الذي وضع له اللفظ أصلاً وبين المعنى الآخر المراد من اللفظ، وإلا لكان استعمالاً خاطئاً للفظ فى ذلك المعنى، ولا اعتبار به، فلا يجوز مثلاً أن يطلق سلفى لفظ الإله ويريد به معنى الجسم، لأن لفظ الإله لا يدل على معنى الجسم بالمطابقة قطعـاً حيث لم يوضع لفظ الإله لمعنى الجسم، وكذا لا يدل عليه بالتضمن قطعاً لأن الجسمية ليست جزء معنى الإله، معنى الإله هو المستغنى عن كل ما سواه والمحتاج إليه كل ما عداه ومن كانت هذه حقيقتـه سبحانه لا يتصور فيه التجزؤ، لأنه ليس بكل مفتقر إلى أجزائه، لأنه لا يفتقر إلى شيء مطلقاً. وكذا لا يدل عليه بالالتزام لأن الجسمية نعم هى خارجة عن حقيقة الإله ولكنها ليست لازمة من لوازم معناه. وعليه بطل إطلاق الإله على الجسم. و زيادة فى بيان دلالة الالتزام نقول: هي دلالة اللفظ الموضوع لمعنى معين على معنى آخر خارج عن المعنى الذى وضع اللفظ له أصلاً، ولكن هذا المعنى الخارج عن =معنی اللفظ لازم لمعنى اللفظ الوضع. ففى دلالة الالتزام ترى لفظاً دالاً على معنى غير المعنى الذى وضع له اللفظ، ولكنه لازم لذلك المعنى الوضعي الأصلى بحسب
Know that the word signifying by positing a specific meaning either indicates the entirety of that meaning—i.e., it indicates that meaning itself in its entirety such that nothing of the parts of the meaning that the positer considered and observed in exchange for the word is left out—or it does not indicate the entirety of that meaning. If the word indicates the entirety of the meaning posited for it, that verbal posited indication is called indication by correspondence (dalālat muṭābaqa), because of the correspondence, i.e., agreement, between the word and the meaning. An example is the indication of 'human' on 'rational animal', and 'horse' on 'whinnying animal', and so forth. Note that indication by correspondence can be in a composite meaning, as in the indication of 'human' on 'rational animal', which is a meaning composed of animality and rationality, and it can be in a meaning in which composition and division are not conceivable, as we say the word 'atom' (jawhar fard) indicates the indivisible part, which is a simple, non-compound meaning. Likewise, when we utter the beautiful names of Allah the Exalted upon Him, they indicate the Most Holy Essence, the Necessary Existence, the Independent, the Transcendent, the Exalted above attributes of deficiency and temporal origination, such as composition and partition and similar things not conceivable in the Eternal. Also know that correspondence occurs between a single word and a simple meaning, between a single word and a composite meaning, between a compound expression and a simple meaning, and between a compound expression and a composite meaning. Example of the first: the word of majesty 'Allah' on the Necessary Existence; example of the second: 'human' on rational animal; example of the third: 'Necessary Existence' on al-Ilāh; example of the fourth: the phrase 'principles of jurisprudence' (uṣūl al-fiqh) on the summarized methods of fiqh. As for when the word does not indicate the entirety of the meaning for which it was posited, then either it indicates a part of the meaning posited for it—that is, the meaning for which the word was posited is a composite having two or more parts, so the word indicates a part of the parts of that composite meaning—or it does not indicate even a part of the meaning in exchange for which the word was posited. So if the word indicates a part of the meaning for which this word was posited, the indication is called indication by inclusion (dalālat taḍammun), because the part is within the whole of the meaning posited for it. Note that indication by inclusion can only be conceived in composite meanings, i.e., those having parts, unlike correspondence as I have shown you. Remaining for the completion of the division: the word may indicate a meaning that is neither the entirety of the meaning posited for it nor a part of it; it then necessarily indicates something else outside the reality of the meaning in exchange for which the word was posited, but it is necessary for it. And this division of indication is what they call indication by entailment (dalālat iltizām). In it, there must be a relation of entailment between the meaning for which the word was originally posited and the other meaning intended from the word, otherwise it would be an incorrect usage of the word in that meaning, and it is not considered. For example, it is not permissible for someone to utter the word 'al-Ilāh' (God) and intend by it the meaning of body, because the word 'al-Ilāh' does not indicate the meaning of body by correspondence at all, since the word 'al-Ilāh' was not posited for the meaning of body. Likewise, it does not indicate it by inclusion at all, because bodyness is not a part of the meaning of 'al-Ilāh'. The meaning of 'al-Ilāh' is the one independent of everything other than Him and the one to whom everything else is in need. And whoever has this reality—glorified is He—cannot be conceived to have parts, because He is not a whole dependent on His parts, since He is not dependent on anything at all. Likewise, it does not indicate it by entailment, because bodyness, yes, is outside the reality of 'al-Ilāh', but it is not a necessary concomitant of His meaning. Therefore, applying the word 'al-Ilāh' to body is invalid. And as an addition in clarifying indication by entailment, we say: It is the indication of a word posited for a specific meaning on another meaning outside the meaning for which the word was originally posited, but this outside meaning is necessary to the posited meaning of the word. So in indication by entailment, you see a word indicating a meaning other than the meaning for which the word was posited, but it is necessary to that original posited meaning, according to...
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage from the Muyassar Sullam commentary provides a systematic classification of the three types of verbal indication (dalāla lafẓiyya waḍʿiyya): correspondence (muṭābaqa), inclusion (taḍammun), and entailment (iltizām). The author begins with correspondence: when a word indicates the entire meaning for which it was posited. Examples include 'human' indicating 'rational animal' and 'horse' indicating 'whinnying animal'. The author notes that correspondence can apply to both composite and simple meanings, giving the examples of 'atom' (a simple meaning) and the names of Allah (indicating the simple Essence). The passage then explains that correspondence can occur between various combinations of single/compound words and simple/composite meanings, with examples such as 'Allah' for Necessary Existence (single word, simple meaning), 'human' for rational animal (single word, composite meaning), 'Necessary Existence' for al-Ilāh (compound expression, simple meaning), and 'uṣūl al-fiqh' for the summarized methods of fiqh (compound expression, composite meaning). Next, the author turns to inclusion: when a word indicates a part of its posited meaning. This only applies to composite meanings, as a simple meaning has no parts. Finally, the author addresses entailment: when a word indicates a meaning that is neither the whole nor a part of its posited meaning but is a necessary concomitant of it. This requires a relation of entailment between the original meaning and the associated meaning. The author illustrates this with the theological example that the word 'al-Ilāh' cannot be used to mean 'body', because body is not necessary to the meaning of God, nor is it part of that meaning, nor does it correspond to it. Thus, the classification is exhaustive: every verbal (posited) indication is either mutābaqa, taḍammun, or iltizām. The passage ends with a further clarification that iltizām involves a necessary connection, not any arbitrary association.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is an example of indication by correspondence (muṭābaqa) with a compound expression indicating a composite meaning?
A) The word 'Allah' indicating the Necessary Existence.
B) The word 'human' indicating rational animal.
C) The phrase 'principles of jurisprudence' indicating the summarized methods of fiqh.
D) The word 'horse' indicating the whinnying animal.

Key Takeaway
Indication by correspondence (muṭābaqa) is when a word covers its entire posited meaning, and it can occur in all four combinations of simple/compound words and simple/composite meanings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Identify whether the indication of the word 'sawm' (fasting) in the verse 'Kutiba 'alaykumu al-siyām' is muṭābaqa, taḍammun, or iltizām. Explain why.

Hadd and Rasm
beginner
5 min
Indication by Inclusion (Dalālat al-Taḍammun)
Definition of taḍammun and its restriction to composite meanings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when a word indicates a part of its meaning (taḍammun) and explain why this requires the meaning to be composite.

Core Idea
Inclusion picks out a part of a composite meaning.

When a word does not indicate its entire posited meaning, it may indicate a part of it. This is called indication by inclusion (taḍammun). The author clarifies that this type only applies to composite meanings, as simple meanings have no parts. Through examples, you will learn to distinguish taḍammun from muṭābaqa.

Guided Path
1
Recall the division
The author said verbal indication either indicates the entire meaning or not. For the latter, it may indicate a part or neither part nor whole.
2
Define taḍammun
It is when a word indicates a part of its posited meaning, presupposing that the meaning is composite (has parts).
3
Understand the requirement
Taḍammun cannot occur for simple meanings; it only works for composite ones.
4
Contrast with muṭābaqa
Note that muṭābaqa can be for both simple and composite, but taḍammun is restricted to composite.
