The Two Methods of Definition: Hadd and Rasm
Author introduces two methods of definition: hadd and rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between hadd and rasm and determine which method is appropriate for a given quiddity using examples from Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
Hadd reveals essence through essential properties; rasm distinguishes through accidents.

When we seek to know a quiddity, we can either dive into its essential composition (hadd) or mark it by its distinctive external features (rasm). This lesson unpacks these two foundational methods of definition as presented by the author.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Locate in the passage the general term being defined (المعرفات) or the quiddity for which methods are discussed. The passage defines 'definitions' as composite expressions that reveal or distinguish.
The passage speaks generically about quiddities, so we can apply the methods to any term.
2
Extract the two methods
From the passage, identify: hadd – investigating the quiddity itself to know its essential meanings (المعاني الذاتية); rasm – discovering the accidental things (الأمور الغريبة) that distinguish it from others.
Hadd uses essential properties internal to the quiddity; rasm uses external distinguishing marks.
3
Compare the outcomes
Note that hadd yields both revelation (كشف) of the essence and distinction (تمييز) from others; rasm yields only distinction. The passage states: 'فمعرفة الذاتيات للماهية يترتب عليها أمران... وأما الطريقة الثانية فلا يترتب عليها إلا تمييزها'.
Hadd provides deeper knowledge; rasm is a weaker form of definition.
4
Apply to an Islamic example
Take the quiddity 'salah' (prayer). A hadd would list essential pillars (intention, takbir, recitation, ruku, sujud, taslim). A rasm might describe its accidental features: five times daily, facing qibla, with specific movements. This shows how the two methods differ in Islamic practice.
Ensure the hadd includes only essential constituents; the rasm uses distinctive but non-essential properties.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فضل في المعرفات 
بيان المعاني الكلية والألفاظ الدالة عليها ، يعتبره العلماء مقدمة آلية يلزم تحقيقها لتأليف الأقوال الشارحة التي تبين للمريد مفاهيم الماهيات المطلوب له معرفتها.
وهذه الأقوال الشارحة تسمى (معرّفات)، وسوف نبين أقسام المعرفات في هذا الفصل.
عندما نريد أن نعرف بعض الماهيات، فإن هناك طريقتين لتحقيق ذلك:
إما أن نسلط نظرنا على نفس الماهية، فنعمل فيها بعض طرق البحث والنظر من سبر وتقسيم، حتى نعلم من ماذا تتألف، أي ما هي المعاني الذاتية التي تتألف منها، وتسمى هذه الطريقة بالحدّ. أو أن تعمل نظرنا للكشف عن الأمور التي تميزها عن غيرها من الماهيات والأمور الغريبة عنها، وتسمى هذه الطريقة بالرسم.
فإننا إن استطعنا معرفة المعاني الذاتية لها، تتحقق معرفتنا بها، وبعد معرفتها من هذه الحيثية تتميز عندنا حداً. وإن استطعنا معرفة الأمور التي تميزها عن غيرها يتحقق تمييزنا لها أيضاً ولكن رسماً. فالمعرفات عبارة عن ألفاظ مركبة تركيباً تقييداً تحمل بياناً كاشفاً أو مميزا (1) عن الماهية المطلوب معرفتها. فمعرفة الذاتيات للماهية يترتب عليها أمران: الأول: الكشف عنها ببيان ذاتياتها ببيان الحد ، والثاني: تمييزها عما عداها ببيان الرسم.
وأما الطريقة الثانية للتعريف فلا يترتب عليها إلا تمييزها عما عداها. ومبحث المعرفات هدفه هو الوصول إلى بيان كيفية التعريف، أي ما هي المعاني التي يجب أن نستعملها لكي نتوصل إلى تعريفها لنا وللغير. وبعد أن نتمكن من صياغة التعريفات بقسميها، نستطيع بعد ذلك أن نستعمل نفس هذه التعريفات للتعليم والتفهيم والمعارف الأخر في البحث والنظر.
ولكن هل الوصول إلى التعريفات، هو أمر بديهي؟ لو كان أمراً بديهياً، لكانت معرفتنا للماهيات كلها بديهية، ولتحقق للكل معرفتها، فانتفى طلب التصورات، ولكن كل هذا باطل. إذن فالمعرفة بالتعريفات ليست كلها بديهية، فبعض الأمور بديهية المعرفة، وبعضها وهو الأغلب ليس بديهياً، بل هو نظري أي يحتاج إلى بحث ونظر للوصول إليه. ويلزمنا أن نذكر مقدمة مختصرة لبيان كيفية النظر اللازم اتباعه للوصول إلى اكتساب التعريفات النظرية.
A chapter on definitions. The explanation of universal concepts and the expressions indicating them is considered by scholars as an instrumental introduction necessary to achieve, for composing explanatory statements that show the seeker the concepts of quiddities that he wants to know. These explanatory statements are called 'definitions', and we will explain the divisions of definitions in this chapter. When we want to define some quiddities, there are two ways to achieve that: either we focus our view on the quiddity itself, employing some methods of investigation and examination such as probing and dividing, until we know what it is composed of, i.e., what are the essential meanings that compose it, and this method is called 'hadd' (definition); or we employ our view to discover the things that distinguish it from other quiddities and the extraneous things, and this method is called 'rasm' (description). For if we are able to know its essential meanings, our knowledge of it is achieved, and after knowing it from this aspect it becomes distinguished for us as a hadd. And if we are able to know the things that distinguish it from others, our distinguishing of it is also achieved, but as a rasm. So definitions are composite expressions with a restrictive composition that carry an explanatory or distinctive (1) statement about the quiddity to be known. Knowing the essential properties of a quiddity results in two things: first, revealing it by stating its essential properties through stating the hadd; second, distinguishing it from what is other than it through stating the rasm. As for the second method of definition, it results only in distinguishing it from what is other than it. The subject of definitions aims to reach an explanation of the how of definition, i.e., what meanings we must use in order to arrive at defining it for ourselves and for others. After we are able to formulate definitions in their two divisions, we can then use these same definitions for teaching, understanding, and other cognitions in investigation and reflection. But is arriving at definitions an intuitive matter? If it were intuitive, our knowledge of all quiddities would be intuitive, and everyone would know them, and the pursuit of concepts would be eliminated, but all this is false. Therefore, knowledge of definitions is not entirely intuitive; some things are intuitively known, and some—which is the majority—are not intuitive but theoretical, i.e., they require investigation and reflection to arrive at. And we must provide a brief introduction explaining the method of reflection that must be followed to acquire theoretical definitions.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an introductory section on definitions (al-mu'arrafat). The author states that the explanation of universal concepts and their expressions is an instrumental preface necessary for composing explanatory statements that clarify quiddities to the seeker. These explanatory statements are called definitions, and the chapter will explain their divisions. Two methods are distinguished for defining quiddities: (1) analyzing the quiddity itself to discover its essential constituents (al-ma'ani al-dhatiyya), which is called hadd (definition proper); (2) discovering the accidental features that distinguish it from others, which is called rasm (description). Both methods yield knowledge: hadd reveals the quiddity's essence, while rasm distinguishes it. Definitions are composite expressions that either reveal or distinguish. The author then explains that knowing the essential properties (dhatiyyat) results in two things: (a) revealing the quiddity by stating its hadd, and (b) distinguishing it by stating its rasm. The second method (rasm) only distinguishes. The aim of the study is to understand how to formulate definitions for oneself and others, and to use them for teaching and further inquiry. The passage then raises the epistemological question: are definitions intuitive? The author argues no—if they were, all quiddities would be known intuitively, which is false. Some things are intuitive, but most are theoretical, requiring investigation. Thus, a method for acquiring theoretical definitions is needed. This sets the stage for discussing the process of definition. The commentary uses examples implicit in the text: hadd would be like defining 'man' as 'rational animal' (essential), while rasm might be 'laughing animal' (distinctive accidental).

Key Terms
المعرفات
الحد
الرسم
المعاني الذاتية
الأمور الغريبة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary outcome of a hadd that is not achieved by a rasm?
A) Hadd reveals the quiddity's essence and distinguishes it; rasm only distinguishes.
B) Hadd is shorter than rasm.
C) Rasm reveals essence; hadd does not.
D) Hadd uses accidents; rasm uses essentials.

Key Takeaway
Hadd defines by essential properties, offering both understanding and differentiation; rasm defines by accidental properties, offering only differentiation.

Are Definitions Intuitive? The Epistemology of Definition
Author argues that definitions are mostly theoretical, not intuitive.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why most definitions are theoretical (nazari) and identify the distinction between intuitive (badihi) and theoretical knowledge using the author's reductio argument.

Core Idea
Not all definitions are intuitive; the majority require effort and method.

The author raises a key epistemological question: can we know definitions without effort? He argues that if all definitions were intuitive, then all quiddities would be known innately, which is false. Therefore, a method for acquiring theoretical definitions is necessary. This lesson unpacks that argument and its implications for the study of definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the question
The author asks directly: 'هل الوصول إلى التعريفات، هو أمر بديهي؟' (Is arriving at definitions intuitive?). This frames the entire argument.
The term 'badihi' means self-evident, requiring no proof.
2
Analyze the conditional consequence
The author posits the consequence: if definitions were intuitive, then all quiddities would be known intuitively (بديهية) and the pursuit of concepts (طلب التصورات) would be unnecessary.
This is a conditional statement: if P (all definitions badihi), then Q (all quiddities known intuitively).
3
Evaluate the premise as false
The author declares this consequence false (باطل) because in reality we do seek and investigate concepts; not everything is known innately.
By denying Q, the argument uses modus tollens: if P then Q, not Q, therefore not P.
4
Distinguish categories
The author concludes that some definitions are badihi, but the majority are theoretical (نظري), requiring research and reflection (بحث ونظر).
Theoretical definitions must be acquired through a methodical process.
5
Understand the need for method
The passage ends by stating the necessity of providing a brief introduction on how to conduct the required investigation to acquire theoretical definitions.
This justifies the entire science of definitions as presented in the chapter.

فضل في المعرفات 
بيان المعاني الكلية والألفاظ الدالة عليها ، يعتبره العلماء مقدمة آلية يلزم تحقيقها لتأليف الأقوال الشارحة التي تبين للمريد مفاهيم الماهيات المطلوب له معرفتها.
وهذه الأقوال الشارحة تسمى (معرّفات)، وسوف نبين أقسام المعرفات في هذا الفصل.
عندما نريد أن نعرف بعض الماهيات، فإن هناك طريقتين لتحقيق ذلك:
إما أن نسلط نظرنا على نفس الماهية، فنعمل فيها بعض طرق البحث والنظر من سبر وتقسيم، حتى نعلم من ماذا تتألف، أي ما هي المعاني الذاتية التي تتألف منها، وتسمى هذه الطريقة بالحدّ. أو أن تعمل نظرنا للكشف عن الأمور التي تميزها عن غيرها من الماهيات والأمور الغريبة عنها، وتسمى هذه الطريقة بالرسم.
فإننا إن استطعنا معرفة المعاني الذاتية لها، تتحقق معرفتنا بها، وبعد معرفتها من هذه الحيثية تتميز عندنا حداً. وإن استطعنا معرفة الأمور التي تميزها عن غيرها يتحقق تمييزنا لها أيضاً ولكن رسماً. فالمعرفات عبارة عن ألفاظ مركبة تركيباً تقييداً تحمل بياناً كاشفاً أو مميزا (1) عن الماهية المطلوب معرفتها. فمعرفة الذاتيات للماهية يترتب عليها أمران: الأول: الكشف عنها ببيان ذاتياتها ببيان الحد ، والثاني: تمييزها عما عداها ببيان الرسم.
وأما الطريقة الثانية للتعريف فلا يترتب عليها إلا تمييزها عما عداها. ومبحث المعرفات هدفه هو الوصول إلى بيان كيفية التعريف، أي ما هي المعاني التي يجب أن نستعملها لكي نتوصل إلى تعريفها لنا وللغير. وبعد أن نتمكن من صياغة التعريفات بقسميها، نستطيع بعد ذلك أن نستعمل نفس هذه التعريفات للتعليم والتفهيم والمعارف الأخر في البحث والنظر.
ولكن هل الوصول إلى التعريفات، هو أمر بديهي؟ لو كان أمراً بديهياً، لكانت معرفتنا للماهيات كلها بديهية، ولتحقق للكل معرفتها، فانتفى طلب التصورات، ولكن كل هذا باطل. إذن فالمعرفة بالتعريفات ليست كلها بديهية، فبعض الأمور بديهية المعرفة، وبعضها وهو الأغلب ليس بديهياً، بل هو نظري أي يحتاج إلى بحث ونظر للوصول إليه. ويلزمنا أن نذكر مقدمة مختصرة لبيان كيفية النظر اللازم اتباعه للوصول إلى اكتساب التعريفات النظرية.
A chapter on definitions. The explanation of universal concepts and the expressions indicating them is considered by scholars as an instrumental introduction necessary to achieve, for composing explanatory statements that show the seeker the concepts of quiddities that he wants to know. These explanatory statements are called 'definitions', and we will explain the divisions of definitions in this chapter. When we want to define some quiddities, there are two ways to achieve that: either we focus our view on the quiddity itself, employing some methods of investigation and examination such as probing and dividing, until we know what it is composed of, i.e., what are the essential meanings that compose it, and this method is called 'hadd' (definition); or we employ our view to discover the things that distinguish it from other quiddities and the extraneous things, and this method is called 'rasm' (description). For if we are able to know its essential meanings, our knowledge of it is achieved, and after knowing it from this aspect it becomes distinguished for us as a hadd. And if we are able to know the things that distinguish it from others, our distinguishing of it is also achieved, but as a rasm. So definitions are composite expressions with a restrictive composition that carry an explanatory or distinctive (1) statement about the quiddity to be known. Knowing the essential properties of a quiddity results in two things: first, revealing it by stating its essential properties through stating the hadd; second, distinguishing it from what is other than it through stating the rasm. As for the second method of definition, it results only in distinguishing it from what is other than it. The subject of definitions aims to reach an explanation of the how of definition, i.e., what meanings we must use in order to arrive at defining it for ourselves and for others. After we are able to formulate definitions in their two divisions, we can then use these same definitions for teaching, understanding, and other cognitions in investigation and reflection. But is arriving at definitions an intuitive matter? If it were intuitive, our knowledge of all quiddities would be intuitive, and everyone would know them, and the pursuit of concepts would be eliminated, but all this is false. Therefore, knowledge of definitions is not entirely intuitive; some things are intuitively known, and some—which is the majority—are not intuitive but theoretical, i.e., they require investigation and reflection to arrive at. And we must provide a brief introduction explaining the method of reflection that must be followed to acquire theoretical definitions.
Source pages p. 39

Commentary
This passage is an introductory section on definitions (al-mu'arrafat). The author states that the explanation of universal concepts and their expressions is an instrumental preface necessary for composing explanatory statements that clarify quiddities to the seeker. These explanatory statements are called definitions, and the chapter will explain their divisions. Two methods are distinguished for defining quiddities: (1) analyzing the quiddity itself to discover its essential constituents (al-ma'ani al-dhatiyya), which is called hadd (definition proper); (2) discovering the accidental features that distinguish it from others, which is called rasm (description). Both methods yield knowledge: hadd reveals the quiddity's essence, while rasm distinguishes it. Definitions are composite expressions that either reveal or distinguish. The author then explains that knowing the essential properties (dhatiyyat) results in two things: (a) revealing the quiddity by stating its hadd, and (b) distinguishing it by stating its rasm. The second method (rasm) only distinguishes. The aim of the study is to understand how to formulate definitions for oneself and others, and to use them for teaching and further inquiry. The passage then raises the epistemological question: are definitions intuitive? The author argues no—if they were, all quiddities would be known intuitively, which is false. Some things are intuitive, but most are theoretical, requiring investigation. Thus, a method for acquiring theoretical definitions is needed. This sets the stage for discussing the process of definition. The commentary uses examples implicit in the text: hadd would be like defining 'man' as 'rational animal' (essential), while rasm might be 'laughing animal' (distinctive accidental).

نظري
طلب التصورات

Method of Constructing Definitions: Analysis of Khamr
Author explains the method of tarkib (composition) to define theoretical concepts, using khamr as an example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of tarkib to construct a hadd or rasm for a given concept by analyzing its attributes and identifying the proximate genus and differentia.

Core Idea
A definition is built by analyzing a particular into essential attributes, then selecting the nearest genus and differentia.

In this passage, the author explains how to construct a definition for a theoretical concept using the method of composition (tarkib). The example of khamr (wine) illustrates the step-by-step process of analyzing a particular instance, classifying its attributes, and arriving at a concise hadd. Understanding this method is crucial for precise definitions in any Islamic science.

Guided Path
1
Take a particular instance
Choose a concrete example of the concept to be defined. The author uses a specific khamr (wine) as the instance.
2
Analyze into constituent attributes
List all observable attributes of the instance. For khamr: red color, foaming, pungent odor, intoxicating, body, fluid, liquid, drink, pressed from grapes.
3
Classify attributes: essential vs. accidental vs. concomitant
Determine which attributes are essential (dhati: necessary for conception), accidental ('aradi: not necessary), or necessary concomitant (lazim: necessarily accompanies but not part of essence). The author identifies red color and foaming as accidental; pungent odor and intoxicating property as concomitant; the rest as essential.
Essential attributes are those without which the thing cannot be conceived.
4
Eliminate redundant attributes
Among essential attributes, drop those that are implied by more specific ones. For example, 'body' is dropped because 'liquid' implies it; 'fluid' and 'liquid' are synonyms so one suffices; 'drink' implies fluid so keep 'drink'. Remaining: drink, pressed from grapes, intoxicating.
Keep only the most specific essential attributes.
5
Extract the proximate genus and differentia
The proximate genus (jins qarib) is the broad category shared with other species. Here 'drink' is the genus. The differentia (fasl) is the distinguishing essential attribute: 'intoxicating'. This separates khamr from other drinks like juice or water.
The genus must be the nearest one common to other species.

Source Text

إن الطريقة لاكتساب التصورات ومعرفة الماهيات النظرية هي طريقة التركيب. وذلك بأن نأخذ شخصاً من المراد تعريفها، فنحللها إلى الصفات المتألفة منها، ثم نميز بين العرضى واللازم والذاتي فإن أردنا أن نحدها، اعتبرنا الذاتيات، وإن أرنا أن نرسمها اعتبرنا ما سواها. ثم نرتبها الترتيب الصحيح بأن نبدأ من الأعلى إلى الأخص (3) ونقتصر على الأخير القريب، ونضيف إليه الفصل. مثال ذلك إذا أردنا تعريف الخمر: فإننا أولاً نأخذ خمراً معيناً، فنلاحظ أنها ذات لون أحمر، ويقذف بالزبد، ونراه ذا رائحة حادة مطرباً للشارب. ونراه جسماً أو مائعاً وسيالاً، وشراباً مسكراً، ومعتصراً من العنب.
فأما اللون الأحمر وكونه يقذف بالزبد ، فإنها ليست ذاتيات، لأن بعض ما هو أحمر ويقذف بالزبد ليس خمراً. وأما الرائحة الحادة وكونه مطرباً للشارب، فهذه ليس داخلة في الخمر ، ولكنها لازمة عن الخمر، بدليل أننا نتصور الخمر دون أن نستحضر هذين الوصفين ولا يضر ذلك في تصورنا للخمر. وأيضاً فإنها قد يشترك مع الخمر فيها غيرها. وأما الجسمية وكونه مائعاً ،وسيالاً وشراباً ،ومسكراً، ومعتصراً من العنب. فهذه الصفات ذاتية للخمر، لأننا لا نستطيع أن نتصور الخمر إلا بتصورها ، واستحضارها. ولكن بعضها قد يغني عن البعض، فكل سيال ،جسم فالسيال أخص من الجسم. فنسقط الجسمية والسيال والمائع متساويان، فنستغني بواحد عن الآخر. ثم الشراب يجب أن يكون مائعاً. فنستغني به عنه، فيبقى الشراب، وكونه معتصراً من العنب، وكونه مسكراً.
،
فنأخذ الجنس القريب، وهو شراب، لأنه مشترك بين الخمر وبين غيرها. ثم نقيده بفصل يفصلها عن غيرها. فنقول: مسكر.
فالحاصل أن الخمر: شراب مسكر.
ثم ننظر لنتأكد هل هذا الحد يساوي حقيقتها ، فإن ساواها اكتفينا به، وإلا أضفنا إليه ما يتممه.
(4)
فهذه هي الطريق للحصول على الحدود وغيرها من التعريفات بحسب الإمكان البشري في كل مطلوب.
(1) أى سواء مع اعتبارنا لبعض الذاتيات كما في الرسم التام أو لا مع اعتبارنا لبعضها كما في الرسم الناقص.
(2) أى الأجزاء التى حصلنا عليها من التحليل. (3) أى من الأعلى الأعم إلى الأدنى الأخص.
(4) لأن التعريف يكون بحسب الطاقة البشرية، ولا يطلب من التعريف أن يكشف عن المعرف كما هو في نفس الأمر. لأنّ ذلك ليس في وسع البشر. فيجتهد لاقتناص الحد ثمّ بتوالى أنظار العلماء في التعريف والمعرف تتنقح الحدود. وتبقى دائماً ضمن الإمكان البشرى المحدد بالأسباب العادية.
Indeed, the method for acquiring concepts and knowing theoretical essences is the method of composition. That is by taking an individual of what is intended to be defined, analyzing it into the attributes composing it, then distinguishing between accidental, necessary, and essential. If we want to define it by hadd, we consider the essential properties; and if we want to define it by rasm, we consider what is other than them. Then we arrange them in the correct order by starting from the highest (most general) to the most specific (3) and restrict ourselves to the nearest last (proximate genus) and add to it the differentia. An example: if we want to define khamr (wine): first we take a particular khamr, and we notice that it has red color, foams, has a pungent odor, intoxicates the drinker. And we see it as a body or fluid, liquid, intoxicating drink, and pressed from grapes. As for the red color and its foaming, these are not essential because some things that are red and foam are not khamr. As for the pungent odor and its intoxicating property, these are not internal to khamr, but are necessary concomitant of khamr, evidenced by the fact that we conceive khamr without bringing these two descriptions to mind and that does not harm our conception of khamr. Also, others may share in them with khamr. As for corporeality, being fluid, liquid, a drink, intoxicating, and pressed from grapes—these attributes are essential to khamr because we cannot conceive khamr except by conceiving and bringing them to mind. However, some may suffice for others. For every liquid is a body, so liquid is more specific than body. So we drop corporeality; liquid and fluid are equivalent, so we suffice with one over the other. Then drink must be a fluid, so we suffice with it over that. So what remains is drink, being pressed from grapes, and being intoxicating. So we take the proximate genus, which is 'drink', because it is shared between khamr and other things. Then we restrict it with a differentia that separates it from others. We say: 'intoxicating'. So the outcome is: khamr is an intoxicating drink. Then we look to ascertain whether this hadd is equivalent to its reality; if it is equivalent, we suffice with it, otherwise we add to it what completes it. (4) So this is the way to obtain hadd and other definitions according to human capability in every object of inquiry. (1) i.e., whether with consideration of some essential properties as in the complete rasm or without consideration of some as in the incomplete rasm. (2) i.e., the parts we obtained from analysis. (3) i.e., from the highest most general to the lowest most specific. (4) Because definition is according to human capacity; it is not required that the definition reveal the defined object as it is in itself, because that is beyond human ability. So one strives to capture the hadd, then through successive views of scholars on the definition and the defined, the definitions are refined. And they always remain within human possibility limited by ordinary means.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage explains the method of acquiring definitions for theoretical concepts. The method is called 'tarkib' (composition). The process: take a particular instance of the thing to be defined, analyze it into its constituent attributes, then classify those attributes into 'aradi' (accidental), 'lazim' (necessary concomitant), and 'dhati' (essential). If the goal is a hadd (essential definition), we consider only the essential properties. If the goal is a rasm (descriptive definition), we consider the non-essential distinguishing properties. Then we arrange the essential properties in order from the most general to the most specific, restrict ourselves to the nearest genus (jins qarib), and add the differentia (fasl). The author illustrates with the example of khamr (wine). First, we take a particular wine and observe its attributes: red color, foaming, pungent odor, intoxicating, being a body, fluid, liquid, a drink, pressed from grapes. Then we evaluate each: red color and foaming are not essential because some red foaming things are not wine. Pungent odor and intoxicating property are necessary concomitants (lazim) — they accompany wine but we can conceive wine without them, and they are shared by other things. The remaining attributes (corporeality, fluidity, liquidity, being a drink, intoxicating, pressed from grapes) are essential because we cannot conceive wine without them. However, some are redundant: liquidity implies corporeality, so we drop corporeality; fluid and liquid are synonyms, so one suffices; drink implies fluid, so we keep 'drink'. The remaining essential properties are: drink, pressed from grapes, and intoxicating. The proximate genus common to wine and other things is 'drink'. The differentia that distinguishes wine from other drinks is 'intoxicating'. Thus, the definition (hadd) is 'khamr is an intoxicating drink'. Then we check if this definition corresponds exactly to the reality of wine; if so, we accept it; otherwise, we add what completes it. The passage concludes that this is the humanly possible method for obtaining definitions. The footnotes clarify: in a complete rasm, some essential properties are included; in an incomplete rasm, none. The parts come from analysis. The order is from most general to most specific. The final note emphasizes that definitions are always within human capability and are refined over time by scholars; they need not reveal the essence as it is in itself.

Key Terms
التركيب (al-tarkib)
الجنس القريب (al-jins al-qarib)
الفصل (al-fasl)
العرضي (al-'aradi)
اللازم (al-lazim)

Key Takeaway
The method of tarkib involves analyzing a particular, classifying attributes, and selecting the nearest genus and differentia to construct a valid definition.

The Method of Definition by Analysis and Composition
Author explains the method of definition by analysis and composition using the example of khamr.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the method of tahlil and tarkib to construct a complete definition (hadd) for any term from the Islamic sciences.

Core Idea
A proper definition is built by analyzing a particular instance into essential attributes and composing them into a genus and differentia.

This lesson presents the practical method used by logicians to arrive at definitions. The author walks through the process step by step using the example of wine (khamr), showing how to sift through observed properties and identify those that truly define the essence. You will learn to distinguish essential attributes from accidental ones and to compose them into a correct definition.

Guided Path
1
Take a particular instance
Start with a concrete example of the thing you want to define. In the passage, the author takes a specific sample of wine.
The instance must be representative of the species.
2
List all observed attributes
Write down every property you observe or know about that instance. The author lists: red color, foaming, sharp odor, intoxication, corporeality, liquidity, fluidity, being a beverage, and being pressed from grapes.
3
Classify attributes as essential, necessary, or accidental
Determine which properties are essential (dhati): without them the thing cannot be conceived. Necessary (lazim) properties always accompany the essence but are not part of it. Accidental ('aradi) properties can be absent. The author identifies color and foaming as accidental; odor and intoxication as necessary; and the remaining as essential.
The test is whether you can conceive of the thing without the property.
4
Eliminate redundancies and order from general to specific
Among the essential attributes, some are subsumed by others. Order them from the most general (e.g., body) to the most specific, dropping any that are implied by a more specific attribute. The author drops body because fluid is more specific, and drops liquid because beverage implies liquid.
5
Identify the proximate genus and differentia
The highest remaining attribute that is common to other species is the proximate genus (here, 'beverage'). The specific attribute that distinguishes this species from others is the differentia (here, 'intoxicating'). Combine them: 'Wine is an intoxicating beverage.'
Then verify whether this definition matches the essence completely.

The method for acquiring conceptualizations and knowing theoretical essences is the method of composition. That is by taking a particular instance of what is to be defined, analyzing it into its constituent attributes, then distinguishing between accidental, necessary, and essential. If we want to define it by a complete definition (hadd), we consider the essential properties; if we want to define it by a description (rasm), we consider what is other than them. Then we arrange them in the correct order by starting from the highest [most general] to the most specific, and we restrict [the arrangement] to the last proximate [genus], and we add to it the differentia. Example: if we want to define wine (khamr): we first take a particular wine, and we observe that it has a red color, foams, has a sharp odor, and intoxicates the drinker. And we see it as a body or a liquid, fluid, a beverage, intoxicating, and pressed from grapes. As for the red color and its foaming, they are not essential, because some things that are red and foam are not wine. As for the sharp odor and its intoxicating the drinker, these are not intrinsic to wine, but are necessary properties of wine, evidenced by the fact that we can conceive of wine without recalling these two attributes and that does not harm our conception of wine. Also, other things share these with wine. As for corporeality, being liquid, fluid, beverage, intoxicating, and pressed from grapes—these are essential attributes of wine, because we cannot conceive of wine without conceiving and recalling them. But some suffice for others: every fluid is a body, so fluid is more specific than body. So we drop corporeality; fluid and liquid are equivalent, so we suffice with one over the other. Then beverage must be liquid, so we suffice with it over liquid, so beverage remains, along with being pressed from grapes and being intoxicating. Then we take the proximate genus, which is beverage, because it is common between wine and other things. Then we qualify it with a differentia that distinguishes it from others: we say 'intoxicating.' So the result: wine is an intoxicating beverage. Then we check whether this definition equals its reality; if it equals it, we suffice with it; otherwise, we add what completes it. This is the way to obtain definitions (hudud) and other descriptions according to human capacity in every inquiry. (1) Meaning: whether with consideration of some essential properties as in the complete description, or without consideration of some as in the incomplete description. (2) Meaning: the parts we obtained from analysis. (3) Meaning: from the highest, most general to the lowest, most specific. (4) Because definition is according to human capacity, and definition is not required to reveal the definiendum as it is in itself, because that is beyond human capability. So one strives to capture the definition, then through successive views of scholars on definition and the defined, the definitions are refined, and they remain always within human capacity limited by normal causes.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an exposition of the method for constructing definitions (hudud) and descriptions (rusum). The author begins by stating that the method is 'composition' (tarkib), which involves taking a particular instance of what is to be defined and analyzing it into its attributes. Then one must distinguish between accidental properties ('aradi), necessary properties (lazim), and essential properties (dhati). If one wants a complete definition (hadd), only essential properties are considered; if a description (rasm), non-essential properties are used. After analysis, the attributes are arranged from the most general to the most specific, stopping at the proximate genus and adding the differentia (fasl). The example of wine (khamr) is given to illustrate the process. The author lists various attributes of wine: red color, foaming, sharp odor, intoxication, corporeality, liquidity, fluidity, being a beverage, and being pressed from grapes. He then eliminates non-essential and redundant attributes: red color and foaming are accidental (not exclusive to wine); sharp odor and intoxication are necessary (lazim) but not intrinsic, as wine can be conceived without them; the remaining essential attributes are corporeality, liquidity, fluidity, beverage, intoxication, and pressed from grapes. However, some are redundant: fluid is more specific than body, so body is dropped; liquid and fluid are equivalent, so one suffices; beverage subsumes liquid, so only beverage, pressing from grapes, and intoxication remain. The proximate genus is 'beverage' (sharab), common to wine and other drinks, and the differentia is 'intoxicating' (muskir), resulting in the definition: 'wine is an intoxicating beverage.' The author emphasizes that definitions are according to human capacity and may be refined by scholars over time.

A proper definition in Islamic logic is constructed by analyzing a particular instance into its essential attributes, removing redundancies, and composing the proximate genus with its specific differentia.

The Three Types of Definitions: Hadd, Rasm, and Lafzi
Classification of definitions into three types

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three types of definitions (hadd, rasm, lafzi) based on their components.

Core Idea
Hadd gives essence via genus+differentia; rasm identifies via genus+property; lafzi swaps a synonym.

In Islamic logic, definitions are precise tools, not mere explanations. The poem classifies them into three kinds. Let's examine each type closely.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three types
The poem states the definer divides into three: hadd (essential), rasmi (descriptive), and lafzi (verbal). Locate these terms in the Arabic.
2
Analyze the components of hadd
Hadd is composed of genus (jins) and differentia (fasl). This gives the essence of the thing defined.
Example: 'Human is a rational animal' – genus: animal, differentia: rational.
3
Analyze the components of rasm
Rasm uses genus (jins) and a special property (khāṣṣa). It identifies the thing without giving its essence.
Example: 'Human is a laughing animal' – genus: animal, property: laughing.
4
Understand lafzi
Lafzi simply replaces the word with a more famous synonym. It does not add conceptual knowledge.
Example: Defining 'salah' as 'prayer' – mere synonym substitution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُعَرِّفُ إِلى ثَلاثَةِ قُسِمْ حَدٌ وَرَسْمِيٌّ وَلَفْظِيٌّ عُلم
فَالحَدُّ بِالجِنْسِ وَفَضلٍ وَقَعا
وَالرَّسْمُ بِالجِنْسِ وَخاصَّة مَعا وَناقِصُ الحَدٌ بِفَضلٍ أَوْ مَعـا جنْسِ بَعِيدِ لا قَرِيبٍ وَقَعا
وَناقِصُ الرَّسْمِ بِخَاصَّةٍ فَقَدْ أَوْ مَعَ جِئْسٍ أَبْعَدْ قَدِ ارْتَبَط وَمَا بِلَفْظِي لَدَيْهِم شُهرا تبديل لفظ بردف أَشهرا وَشَرْطُ كُلِّ أَنْ يُرى مُطَّرِداً مُنْعَكِساً وَظَاهِراً لا أَبْعَدا
وَلا مُساوِياً وَلا تَجَوَّزا بِلا قَرِينَةٍ بِها تَحَرَّزا
وَلا بِما يُدْرَى بِمَحْدُودٍ وَلا
مُشْتَرِكِ مِنَ القَرِينَةِ خَلا
وَعِنْدَهُم مِنْ جُمْلَةِ المَرْدودِ أَنْ تُدْخَلَ الأحْكامُ في الحُدُودِ
وَلا يَجُوزُ فِي الحُدُودِ ذِكْرُ أَوْ وَجَائِزٌ فِي الرَّسْمِ فَادْرِ ما رَوَوْا
The definer is divided into three types: hadd (essential definition), rasmi (descriptive definition), and lafzi (verbal definition), it is known. So the essential definition (hadd) occurs by genus and differentia. And the descriptive definition (rasm) occurs by genus and property (khassa) together. An incomplete essential definition occurs by a differentia alone or by a distant genus instead of a proximate one. An incomplete descriptive definition occurs by a property alone or connected with a more distant genus. As for the verbal (lafzi), among them it is well-known as replacing a word with a more famous synonym. The condition of every [definition] is that it be seen as coextensive (muttarid), convertible (mun‘akis), and clear (zahir), not obscure (ab‘ad). Not equivalent (musawi), and not figurative without a qarina (contextual indicator) by which one is cautious. Not by what is known by the definiendum, and not by a homonym (mushtarak) devoid of a qarina. And according to them, among what is rejected is that rulings (ahkam) be included in definitions. And it is not permitted in definitions to mention 'or' (aw), but it is permitted in descriptions, so understand what they narrated.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This is a matn (poetic summary) that classifies definitions into three categories. The first is hadd (essential definition), which is composed of genus (jins) and differentia (fasl). The second is rasmi (descriptive definition), which uses genus and a special property (khāṣṣa). Within each, there are complete (tāmm) and incomplete (nāqiṣ) versions: incomplete hadd uses only the differentia or a distant genus (instead of proximate), while incomplete rasm uses only a property or a more distant genus. The third is lafzi (verbal definition), which merely substitutes a more famous synonym. The poem then lists conditions for all definitions: they must be muttarid (coextensive, applying to all and only the definiendum), mun‘akis (convertible, i.e., the definition and definiendum are interchangeable), and zāhir (clear, not more obscure than the definiendum). They must not be musāwi (equivalent? possibly meaning tautological), nor figurative without a qarīna (contextual indicator). They must not rely on what is known only through the definiendum (circular), nor use ambiguous homonyms without clarification. Additionally, it is rejected to include judgments (ahkām) in definitions, and the word 'or' (aw) is not allowed in hadd but is allowed in rasm. The poem ends with an exhortation to understand these rules.

رسم
لفظي

Key Takeaway
Hadd gives essence (genus+fasl), rasm identifies via property (genus+khassa), lafzi provides a synonym.

Complete and Incomplete Definitions
Complete and incomplete versions of hadd and rasm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify whether a hadd or rasm is complete or incomplete based on its components.

Core Idea
A complete hadd needs proximate genus+differentia; incomplete lacks a component or uses a distant genus.

The poem explains that not all definitions are complete. There are nāqiṣ (incomplete) versions of both hadd and rasm. Let's break down when a definition is considered incomplete.

Guided Path
1
Review complete hadd and rasm
Complete hadd: proximate genus (jins qarīb) + differentia (fasl). Complete rasm: proximate genus + property (khāṣṣa).
2
Identify incomplete hadd
Incomplete hadd occurs in two ways: (a) using only a differentia (no genus), or (b) using a distant genus instead of a proximate one.
Example of (a): 'Human is rational' – missing genus 'animal'.
3
Identify incomplete rasm
Incomplete rasm occurs in two ways: (a) using only a property (no genus), or (b) using a more distant genus (instead of proximate) with a property.
Example of (a): 'Human is laughing' – missing genus 'animal'.
4
Practice classification
Given a definition, decide if it is complete hadd, incomplete hadd, complete rasm, or incomplete rasm based on the presence and proximity of components.
Use examples from fiqh or kalam.

Conditions for Valid Definitions
Conditions for a valid definition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list and apply the conditions that a valid definition must satisfy: coextensiveness, convertibility, clarity, and avoidance of circularity, ambiguity, and rulings.

Core Idea
A definition must be muttarid (cover all) and mun‘akis (cover only) the definiendum, clear, and free from defects.

After classifying definitions, the poem lays down strict conditions that any valid definition must meet. These ensure that the definition actually serves as a precise tool for knowledge. Let's go through them step by step.

Guided Path
1
Condition of coextensiveness (muttarid)
The definition must apply to every instance of the definiendum. No instance of the thing defined should be left out.
Example: 'Man is an animal' is not muttarid because it includes all animals, not just man.
2
Condition of convertibility (mun‘akis)
The definition must apply only to the definiendum. Nothing outside the definiendum should satisfy the definition.
Example: 'Man is a featherless biped' is not mun‘akis because a plucked chicken also fits.
3
Clarity (zahir) and avoidance of obscurity
The definition must be clearer than the definiendum, not more obscure. Also avoid figurative language without a contextual indicator (qarīna).
Do not define 'lion' as 'king of the jungle' (figurative) without qarina.
4
Prohibited elements
Avoid: (a) circularity (using what is known by the definiendum), (b) homonyms without qarina, (c) including rulings (ahkam), (d) using 'or' (aw) in hadd (allowed in rasm).
Example of circular: 'Salah is prayer' (same word). Example of ruling: 'Salah is obligatory'.

Hadd and Rasm

10 min
Three Types of Definitions: Hadd, Rasm, and Lafzi
Author divides definiendum into three types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify any given definition as hadd, rasm, or lafzi, and identify whether it is perfect or deficient.

Core Idea
Definitions are either essential (hadd), descriptive (rasm), or verbal (lafzi) — only hadd reveals essence.

The author begins by dividing the definiendum into three categories. This classification is the foundation for understanding how definitions work in Islamic logic. The poem clearly states the components of each type, and the commentary expands on their perfect and deficient forms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three categories from the matn
The poem says: 'مُعَرِّفُ إِلى ثَلاثَةِ قُسِمْ حَدٌ وَرَسْمِيٌّ وَلَفْظِيٌّ عُلم'. Extract these three: hadd, rasmī, lafẓī.
Hadd is definition proper, rasm is description, lafzi is verbal.
2
Note the components of each type
Hadd uses genus and differentia (الجنس والفضل). Rasm uses genus and property (الجنس والخاصة). Lafzi uses a more famous synonym (تبديل لفظ بردف أشهر).
Perfect hadd requires nearest genus and nearest differentia; deficient hadd lacks one or uses remote genus.
3
Distinguish perfect and deficient for hadd and rasm
The poem describes deficient hadd: by differentia alone or with remote genus. Deficient rasm: by property alone or with remote genus.
Perfect forms include both genus and differentia/property, with genus being the nearest.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأول الخطوات هي سَبرُ المطلوب تعريفه وتحليله إلى صفاته الموصوف بها، ثم امتحان هذه الصفات بحسب تعريفات العارض والذاتي واللازم، وبعد ذلك يتم ترتيب التعريف المطلوب. فمعرفة المعاني الكلية هو أول المهمات في هذا المطلب. ولذلك بين المصنف كيفية تأليف التعريفات، وأننا إذا أردنا الحد فكيف نرتبه وإذا أردنا الرسم فكيف نستخرجه من الكليات، وهكذا، وهو ما يسمونه بأقسام التعريفات. قال: مُعَرِّفُ إِلى ثَلاثَةِ قُسِمْ حَدٌ وَرَسْمِيٌّ وَلَفْظِيٌّ عُلم فَالحَدُّ بِالجِنْسِ وَفَضلٍ وَقَعا وَالرَّسْمُ بِالجِنْسِ وَخاصَّة مَعا وَناقِصُ الحَدٌ بِفَضلٍ أَوْ مَعـا جنْسِ بَعِيدِ لا قَرِيبٍ وَقَعا وَناقِصُ الرَّسْمِ بِخَاصَّةٍ فَقَدْ أَوْ مَعَ جِئْسٍ أَبْعَدْ قَدِ ارْتَبَط وَمَا بِلَفْظِي لَدَيْهِم شُهرا تبْدِيلُ لَفْظُ بِرَديف أَشْهَرا وَشَرْطُ كُلِّ أَنْ يُرى مُطَرداً مُنْعَكِساً وَظَاهِراً لا أَبْعَدا وَلا مُساوِياً وَلا تَجَوَّزا بِلا قَرِيْنَةٍ بِها تَحَرَّزا وَلا بِما يُدْرَى بِمَحْدُودٍ وَلا مُشْتَرِكِ مِنَ القَرِينَةِ خَلا وَعِنْدَهُم مِنْ جُمْلَةِ المَرْدودِ أَنْ تُدْخَلَ الأحْكامُ في الحُدُودِ وَلا يَجُوزُ فِي الحُدُودِ ذِكْرُ أَوْ وَجَائِزٌ فِي الرَّسْمِ فَادْرِ ما رَوَوْا أقول: ينقسم المعرّف إلى ثلاثة أقسام: الأول: الحد وهو قسمان حد تام، وحد ناقص. الثاني: الرسم وهو أيضاً تام وناقص. الثالث: اللفظى. طريقة تأليف الحد التام: نستطيع تأليف الحد التام بعد معرفة الكليات، بأن نأتي أولاً بالجنس القريب ومعه الفصل القريب. مثاله: الإنسان حيوان ناطق]، ومعنى الحيوان: جسم نام حساس متحرك بالإرادة. فالحيوان جنس قريب يشترك فيه الإنسان مع غيره من الحقائق كالفرس والأسد بالصفات الأعلى، فكل هذه تشترك في هذه الصفات المفهومة من كلمة الحيوان، وأما ما يميز الإنسان عن غيره من الحيوانات فهو كلمة الناطق ومعناها: المفكر ولو بالقوة. أي الذي من شأنه إن أراد أن يقع منه التفكير. فزيد مثلاً يمكن أن يفكر، ولـو يفكر في وقت ما فإنه لا ينتفي كونه إنساناً. ولذلك قال العلماء المفكر بالقوة، لا المفكر بالفعل، فلو كان بالفعل لكان كل مَنْ لم يفكر فعلاً وتنجيزاً غير إنسان، وهذا باطل. فقولنا إذن الإنسان حيوان ناطق حد تام ومعنى كونه تاماً، أن كل إنسان فهو داخل فيه، وكل ما هو غير إنسان فهو خارج منه. ومعنى كونه حداً أي أنه يعرفنا بالصفات الذاتية المكونة لماهية الإنسان لا الخارجة عنه.
The first steps are to analyse the thing sought to be defined into its described attributes, then to examine these attributes according to the definitions of accident, essential, and necessary, and after that the required definition is arranged. So knowledge of universal meanings is the first of the important matters in this subject. Therefore the author explained how to compose definitions, and that if we want the definition (hadd) how we arrange it, and if we want the description (rasm) how we extract it from the universals, and so on, and that is what they call ‘sections of definitions’. He said: ‘The definiendum is divided into three: hadd, rasmī, and lafẓī, as is known. The hadd occurs by genus and differentia; the rasm is with genus and property together. The deficient hadd occurs by differentia alone or with a remote genus, not a near one. The deficient rasm has been given by a property alone, or has been connected with a more remote genus. What is called lafẓī among them is the replacement of a word by a more famous synonym. The condition of every [definition] is that it be seen as coextensive, convertible, and apparent, not [too] remote, nor equal [in obscurity], nor metaphorical without a context by which one is cautious, nor by something known by the defined, nor by an ambiguous word devoid of context. And according to them, it is among the rejected things that rulings be included in definitions; and it is not permissible in definitions to mention ‘or’, but it is permissible in the rasm, so understand what they reported.’ I say: The definiendum is divided into three parts: first: hadd, which has two kinds: perfect hadd and deficient hadd. Second: rasm, also perfect and deficient. Third: lafẓī. The method of composing the perfect hadd: We can compose the perfect hadd after knowing the universals, by bringing first the nearest genus and with it the nearest differentia. Its example: ‘Human is a rational animal’. The meaning of ‘animal’ is a growing, sensing, moving-by-will body. So ‘animal’ is a genus in which human shares with other essences like horse and lion in the higher attributes; all these share in these attributes understood from the word ‘animal’. As for what distinguishes human from other animals, it is the word ‘rational’ and its meaning: the thinker, even if only in potentiality; that is, the one whose property is that when he wills, thinking occurs from him. So Zayd, for instance, can think, and even if he does not think at some time, his being human is not negated. Therefore the scholars said: ‘the thinker in potentiality, not the thinker in actuality’. For if it were actuality, everyone who did not think actually and presently would not be human, and that is false. So our saying ‘human is a rational animal’ is a perfect hadd. The meaning of ‘perfect’ is that every human is included in it, and everything not human is excluded from it. The meaning of its being ‘hadd’ is that it makes us know the essential attributes constituting the quiddity of human, not those external to it.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive treatment of definitions (al-ta‘rīf) in logic. It begins by outlining the method of defining: first, analyze the thing to be defined into its attributes; second, test these attributes as to whether they are accident, essential, or necessary; third, arrange the definition. The author emphasizes that knowledge of the five universals is foundational. Then he quotes a poem from the matn that divides definitions into three categories: hadd (definition proper), rasm (description), and lafẓī (verbal definition). Each is further divided into perfect and deficient. The poem also lists conditions for a valid definition: it must be coextensive (muṭṭarid) and convertible (mun‘akis), clear, not too remote, not metaphorical without a context, not circular, and not ambiguous. Including rulings in definitions is rejected, and using 'or' is forbidden in hadd but allowed in rasm. The commentary then expands on the perfect hadd: it must be composed of the nearest genus (al-jins al-qarīb) and the nearest differentia (al-faṣl al-qarīb). The example 'human is a rational animal' is explained in detail. 'Animal' is the nearest genus, defined as a body that grows, senses, and moves by will. 'Rational' (nāṭiq) means 'thinker potentially' (al-mufakkir bi al-quwwa), not actually, because if it were actual, a sleeping person would not be human. The perfect hadd must include every human and exclude every non-human, and it reveals the essential attributes constituting the quiddity. This lesson uses a Fiqh-like example (Zayd) common in Islamic logic texts.

رسم
لفظي
جنس قريب
فصل قريب
ناطق

Checkpoint
According to the passage, the definition 'human is a laughing animal' (using 'laughing' as a property) is an example of which type of definition?
A) Perfect hadd
B) Deficient hadd
C) Perfect rasm
D) Deficient rasm

Key Takeaway
Definitions are divided into three types: hadd (essential), rasm (descriptive), and lafzi (verbal), each with perfect and deficient variants.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Conditions of a Sound Definition
Author lists conditions for a valid definition.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate a definition against the conditions: coextensiveness, convertibility, clarity, non-circularity, non-ambiguity, and prohibition of including rulings and 'or' in hadd.

Core Idea
A valid definition must be coextensive, convertible, clear, non-circular, and free from ambiguity and extraneous elements.

The matn lists several conditions that every definition must satisfy. These are the criteria by which definitions are accepted or rejected. The commentary explains each condition, providing a checklist for evaluating definitions.

Guided Path
1
Extract the conditions from the poem
The poem states: 'وَشَرْطُ كُلِّ أَنْ يُرى مُطَرداً مُنْعَكِساً وَظَاهِراً لا أَبْعَدا وَلا مُساوِياً وَلا تَجَوَّزا بِلا قَرِيْنَةٍ بِها تَحَرَّزا وَلا بِما يُدْرَى بِمَحْدُودٍ وَلا مُشْتَرِكِ مِنَ القَرِينَةِ خَلا' Also: 'وَلا يَجُوزُ فِي الحُدُودِ ذِكْرُ أَوْ'.
Conditions: coextensive (muṭṭarid), convertible (mun‘akis), apparent (ẓāhir), not too remote, not equal in obscurity, not metaphorical without context, not circular, not ambiguous, no rulings in definitions, no 'or' in hadd.
2
Understand each condition with examples
For each condition, think of a violation: e.g., 'human is a featherless biped' is not convertible (includes plucked birds). The passage forbids including rulings, so 'wine is haram because it intoxicates' is invalid as a definition.
Focus on conditions most relevant to Islamic sciences: coextensiveness and convertibility are critical.
3
Apply conditions to a sample definition
Take the definition 'Salat is specific acts that prevent immorality'. Check coextensiveness: all salat prevents? Not always. Check convertibility: only salat prevents? No, other acts also prevent. Thus it fails.
This shows why conditions are necessary.

Perfect Hadd: The Example of 'Human is a Rational Animal'
Author explains perfect hadd with example.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct a perfect hadd by identifying the nearest genus and nearest differentia for any definiendum, and verify its perfection.

Core Idea
The perfect hadd reveals the essence by combining the immediate genus with the immediate differentia, as in 'human is a rational animal'.

The commentator provides a detailed example of a perfect hadd: 'human is a rational animal'. This example illustrates the method of composing a definition that is both coextensive and convertible. Understanding this example is key to mastering the art of definition in Islamic logic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the nearest genus (jins qarīb)
The nearest genus of human is 'animal' (ḥayawān). It is the immediate category that encompasses humans, horses, lions, etc.
The commentator defines animal as 'a body that grows, senses, and moves by will'.
2
Identify the nearest differentia (faṣl qarīb)
The differentia is 'rational' (nāṭiq), meaning potentially thinking (mufakkir bi al-quwwa). It distinguishes humans from all other animals.
It is potential, not actual, to include sleeping persons.
3
Verify coextensiveness (muṭṭarid) and convertibility (mun‘akis)
Check that every human is included ('all humans are rational animals') and that only humans are included ('only humans are rational animals').
The commentator explicitly states: 'كل إنسان فهو داخل فيه، وكل ما هو غير إنسان فهو خارج منه'.
4
Understand the role of potentiality (bi al-quwwa)
The differentia is 'thinker in potentiality' to avoid excluding those not currently thinking (e.g., asleep, ignorant).
If it were actual, a sleeping person would not be human, which is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فأول الخطوات هي سَبرُ المطلوب تعريفه وتحليله إلى صفاته الموصوف بها، ثم امتحان هذه الصفات بحسب تعريفات العارض والذاتي واللازم، وبعد ذلك يتم ترتيب التعريف المطلوب. فمعرفة المعاني الكلية هو أول المهمات في هذا المطلب. ولذلك بين المصنف كيفية تأليف التعريفات، وأننا إذا أردنا الحد فكيف نرتبه وإذا أردنا الرسم فكيف نستخرجه من الكليات، وهكذا، وهو ما يسمونه بأقسام التعريفات. قال: مُعَرِّفُ إِلى ثَلاثَةِ قُسِمْ حَدٌ وَرَسْمِيٌّ وَلَفْظِيٌّ عُلم فَالحَدُّ بِالجِنْسِ وَفَضلٍ وَقَعا وَالرَّسْمُ بِالجِنْسِ وَخاصَّة مَعا وَناقِصُ الحَدٌ بِفَضلٍ أَوْ مَعـا جنْسِ بَعِيدِ لا قَرِيبٍ وَقَعا وَناقِصُ الرَّسْمِ بِخَاصَّةٍ فَقَدْ أَوْ مَعَ جِئْسٍ أَبْعَدْ قَدِ ارْتَبَط وَمَا بِلَفْظِي لَدَيْهِم شُهرا تبْدِيلُ لَفْظُ بِرَديف أَشْهَرا وَشَرْطُ كُلِّ أَنْ يُرى مُطَرداً مُنْعَكِساً وَظَاهِراً لا أَبْعَدا وَلا مُساوِياً وَلا تَجَوَّزا بِلا قَرِيْنَةٍ بِها تَحَرَّزا وَلا بِما يُدْرَى بِمَحْدُودٍ وَلا مُشْتَرِكِ مِنَ القَرِينَةِ خَلا وَعِنْدَهُم مِنْ جُمْلَةِ المَرْدودِ أَنْ تُدْخَلَ الأحْكامُ في الحُدُودِ وَلا يَجُوزُ فِي الحُدُودِ ذِكْرُ أَوْ وَجَائِزٌ فِي الرَّسْمِ فَادْرِ ما رَوَوْا أقول: ينقسم المعرّف إلى ثلاثة أقسام: الأول: الحد وهو قسمان حد تام، وحد ناقص. الثاني: الرسم وهو أيضاً تام وناقص. الثالث: اللفظى. طريقة تأليف الحد التام: نستطيع تأليف الحد التام بعد معرفة الكليات، بأن نأتي أولاً بالجنس القريب ومعه الفصل القريب. مثاله: الإنسان حيوان ناطق]، ومعنى الحيوان: جسم نام حساس متحرك بالإرادة. فالحيوان جنس قريب يشترك فيه الإنسان مع غيره من الحقائق كالفرس والأسد بالصفات الأعلى، فكل هذه تشترك في هذه الصفات المفهومة من كلمة الحيوان، وأما ما يميز الإنسان عن غيره من الحيوانات فهو كلمة الناطق ومعناها: المفكر ولو بالقوة. أي الذي من شأنه إن أراد أن يقع منه التفكير. فزيد مثلاً يمكن أن يفكر، ولـو يفكر في وقت ما فإنه لا ينتفي كونه إنساناً. ولذلك قال العلماء المفكر بالقوة، لا المفكر بالفعل، فلو كان بالفعل لكان كل مَنْ لم يفكر فعلاً وتنجيزاً غير إنسان، وهذا باطل. فقولنا إذن الإنسان حيوان ناطق حد تام ومعنى كونه تاماً، أن كل إنسان فهو داخل فيه، وكل ما هو غير إنسان فهو خارج منه. ومعنى كونه حداً أي أنه يعرفنا بالصفات الذاتية المكونة لماهية الإنسان لا الخارجة عنه.
The first steps are to analyse the thing sought to be defined into its described attributes, then to examine these attributes according to the definitions of accident, essential, and necessary, and after that the required definition is arranged. So knowledge of universal meanings is the first of the important matters in this subject. Therefore the author explained how to compose definitions, and that if we want the definition (hadd) how we arrange it, and if we want the description (rasm) how we extract it from the universals, and so on, and that is what they call ‘sections of definitions’. He said: ‘The definiendum is divided into three: hadd, rasmī, and lafẓī, as is known. The hadd occurs by genus and differentia; the rasm is with genus and property together. The deficient hadd occurs by differentia alone or with a remote genus, not a near one. The deficient rasm has been given by a property alone, or has been connected with a more remote genus. What is called lafẓī among them is the replacement of a word by a more famous synonym. The condition of every [definition] is that it be seen as coextensive, convertible, and apparent, not [too] remote, nor equal [in obscurity], nor metaphorical without a context by which one is cautious, nor by something known by the defined, nor by an ambiguous word devoid of context. And according to them, it is among the rejected things that rulings be included in definitions; and it is not permissible in definitions to mention ‘or’, but it is permissible in the rasm, so understand what they reported.’ I say: The definiendum is divided into three parts: first: hadd, which has two kinds: perfect hadd and deficient hadd. Second: rasm, also perfect and deficient. Third: lafẓī. The method of composing the perfect hadd: We can compose the perfect hadd after knowing the universals, by bringing first the nearest genus and with it the nearest differentia. Its example: ‘Human is a rational animal’. The meaning of ‘animal’ is a growing, sensing, moving-by-will body. So ‘animal’ is a genus in which human shares with other essences like horse and lion in the higher attributes; all these share in these attributes understood from the word ‘animal’. As for what distinguishes human from other animals, it is the word ‘rational’ and its meaning: the thinker, even if only in potentiality; that is, the one whose property is that when he wills, thinking occurs from him. So Zayd, for instance, can think, and even if he does not think at some time, his being human is not negated. Therefore the scholars said: ‘the thinker in potentiality, not the thinker in actuality’. For if it were actuality, everyone who did not think actually and presently would not be human, and that is false. So our saying ‘human is a rational animal’ is a perfect hadd. The meaning of ‘perfect’ is that every human is included in it, and everything not human is excluded from it. The meaning of its being ‘hadd’ is that it makes us know the essential attributes constituting the quiddity of human, not those external to it.
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive treatment of definitions (al-ta‘rīf) in logic. It begins by outlining the method of defining: first, analyze the thing to be defined into its attributes; second, test these attributes as to whether they are accident, essential, or necessary; third, arrange the definition. The author emphasizes that knowledge of the five universals is foundational. Then he quotes a poem from the matn that divides definitions into three categories: hadd (definition proper), rasm (description), and lafẓī (verbal definition). Each is further divided into perfect and deficient. The poem also lists conditions for a valid definition: it must be coextensive (muṭṭarid) and convertible (mun‘akis), clear, not too remote, not metaphorical without a context, not circular, and not ambiguous. Including rulings in definitions is rejected, and using 'or' is forbidden in hadd but allowed in rasm. The commentary then expands on the perfect hadd: it must be composed of the nearest genus (al-jins al-qarīb) and the nearest differentia (al-faṣl al-qarīb). The example 'human is a rational animal' is explained in detail. 'Animal' is the nearest genus, defined as a body that grows, senses, and moves by will. 'Rational' (nāṭiq) means 'thinker potentially' (al-mufakkir bi al-quwwa), not actually, because if it were actual, a sleeping person would not be human. The perfect hadd must include every human and exclude every non-human, and it reveals the essential attributes constituting the quiddity. This lesson uses a Fiqh-like example (Zayd) common in Islamic logic texts.

Key Terms
حد تام
جنس قريب
فصل قريب
ناطق
بالقوة
بالفعل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The perfect hadd is composed of the nearest genus and nearest differentia; it must be coextensive and convertible, and the differentia must be essential and potentially present.

Hadd and Rasm

The Structure of a Complete Rasm
Author explains how to form a complete rasm by joining near genus and specific property, and discusses the meaning of rasm.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and construct a complete rasm using the near genus and a specific property, and explain why the property is accidental.

Core Idea
A complete rasm describes a thing by its effects, not its essence.

In this passage, the author explains the second type of complete definition: the rasm. Unlike hadd, which captures the essence, rasm describes a thing through its unique accidental properties. The example 'man is a laughing animal' shows how to combine the near genus with a specific property. But is laughter really unique? The author anticipates an objection about monkeys and demonstrates how to defend the definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the near genus and specific property
Find the genus (jins qarib) and the khassa (specific property) in the example 'Man is a laughing animal'. The genus is 'animal', the property is 'laughing'.
2
Check if the property is accidental
Apply the test: Is conception of the property necessary to conceive the definiendum? The author says we can conceive 'man' without conceiving 'laughter', so it is accidental ('aradi), not essential (dhati).
3
Verify uniqueness of the property
Defend against counterexamples. The author refutes the objection that monkeys laugh by distinguishing true laughter (requiring intellect and ta'ajjub) from mere movement. This ensures the khassa is unique to humans.
4
Distinguish rasm from hadd
Compare with the earlier lesson on hadd: hadd uses genus and differentia (essence), while rasm uses genus and accidental property. Recognize that both are complete if they include the near genus and the proper differentiator.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
يمكن تأليف الرسم بأن نأتي بالجنس القريب والخاصة مجتمعين كما في قولنا الإنسان حيوان ضاحك (1) بالقوة. فالضحك للإنسان ليس من ماهيته، ولكنه لازم عنها من أثرها. (2) ومعنى الرسم هو الأثر، فيمكننا أن نعرف الشيء بأثره اللازم عنه، المختص به، ولذلك سمى المناطقة هذه الطريقة بالرسم، ومعنى التام عرفناه. (1) والدليل على أنه ليس من ماهيّته أنه لا يشترط تصوّره لتصوّر الإنسان. مما يدل على أنه خارج عنها، فهو إذاً عرضي لا ذاتي، كما مر. ولا يرد أن القرد يضحك، لأن القرد يحرك شفتيه على صورة المبتسم، أو يفتح فمه ويصدر صوتاً على صورة الضاحك، ولكنه لا يتعجب، لأنه لا يعقل، والتعجب لا يكون إلا للعاقل. (2) أى لغة. وما يليه جاء به لبيان مناسبة تسمية هذا القسم من التعريف رسماً.
It is possible to compose the rasm by bringing together the near genus and the specific property together, as in our saying: 'Man is a laughing animal' (1) potentially. For laughter in man is not from his quiddity, but is a necessary concomitant from its effect. (2) And the meaning of 'rasm' is 'effect', so we can know a thing by its necessary effect which is specific to it. That is why the logicians called this method 'rasm'. And we already know the meaning of 'tam' (complete). (1) The proof that it is not from his quiddity is that its conception is not required for the conception of man. This indicates that it is outside it, so it is accidental ('aradi) not essential (dhati), as has passed. And it cannot be objected that the monkey laughs, because the monkey moves its lips in the form of a smiler, or opens its mouth and makes a sound in the form of a laugher, but it does not wonder (ta'ajjub), because it does not reason, and wonder only occurs from a rational being. (2) i.e., linguistically. And what follows it came to explain the appropriateness of naming this division of definition as 'rasm'.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage explains how to construct a complete rasm (definition by property). The author begins by stating the method: combine the near genus (jins qarib) and the specific property (khassa). The example given is 'Man is a laughing animal'. The laughter is not part of man's quiddity (mahiyya) but a necessary concomitant arising from it. The word 'rasm' literally means 'trace' or 'effect', indicating that we know a thing through its effect. The author then provides a proof that laughter is accidental: its conception is not prerequisite for conceiving man, so it is external to the essence. He also refutes an objection about monkeys laughing, explaining that monkeys lack 'aql (intellect) and true ta'ajjub (wonder), so their behavior is not genuine laughter. This clarifies that the khassa must be unique and necessary.

خاصة
جنس قريب
لازم

Key Takeaway
A complete rasm is built from the near genus and a unique accidental property, and its correctness depends on the property being necessary and exclusive.

Composing an Incomplete Hadd (Naqis)
Author explains the two ways to form an incomplete hadd: using fasl alone or fasl with a distant genus.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to construct an incomplete hadd by either using the fasl alone or combining it with a distant genus, and distinguish it from a complete hadd.

Core Idea
An incomplete hadd omits the near genus but remains permissible and useful.

In the previous lesson, we covered the complete hadd, which requires the near genus and the differentia. However, logicians also recognize a shorter form called the incomplete hadd (hadd naqis), which omits the near genus. In this passage, the author explains the two permissible ways to form an incomplete hadd: using the differentia alone, or using the differentia with a distant genus. This will help you recognize incomplete definitions in logical discourse and understand why they are still acceptable despite missing the near genus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the definiendum
Find the term being defined. In the example 'Man is a speaking body', the definiendum is 'man' (insan).
2
Extract the differentia (fasl)
Locate the property that distinguishes the species. In the example, 'speaking' (natiq) is the differentia.
The differentia should be essential, not accidental.
3
Check if a genus is present
See if the definition includes a genus (jins). If so, identify whether it is a near genus (jins qarib) or a distant genus (jins ba‘id). In the example, 'body' (jism) is a distant genus because a nearer genus ('animal', hayawan) exists.
4
Classify the definition
Decide if it is a complete hadd (near genus + differentia), incomplete hadd (differentia alone, or distant genus + differentia), or a rasm (description). The example is an incomplete hadd.
If no genus appears at all, it is still an incomplete hadd if the differentia is present.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طريقة تأليف الحد الناقص لتأليف الحد الناقص، يمكننا استعمال الفصل وحده، أو الفصل مع جنس بعيد لا قريب. كما في قولنا: الإنسان جسم ناطق. فالناطق فصل كما مضى، والجسم هو جنس بعيد، أي تحته جنس أقرب منه للإنسان وهو الحيوان كما سبق.
Method of composing the incomplete hadd: To compose the incomplete hadd, we can use the differentia alone, or the differentia with a distant genus, not a near one. As in our saying: 'Man is a speaking body'. For 'speaking' is a differentia as has passed, and 'body' is a distant genus, meaning that there is a genus nearer to man than it, which is 'animal', as previously mentioned.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage explains the method of forming an incomplete essential definition (hadd naqis). The author states two possibilities: using the differentia (fasl) alone, or combining the differentia with a distant genus (jins ba'id). The example given is 'Man is a speaking body'. Here 'speaking' is the differentia (fasl), and 'body' is a distant genus because there is a nearer genus, 'animal', which is omitted. This definition is incomplete because it does not include the near genus (jins qarib), which is required for a complete hadd. The point is that while a complete hadd requires near genus and differentia, an incomplete hadd can skip the near genus for brevity or for some rhetorical purpose.

Key Terms
حد ناقص
فصل
جنس بعيد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Man is a rational animal (jins qarib + fasl).
B) Man is a speaking body (jins ba'id + fasl).
C) Man is a laughing animal (jins qarib + khassa).
D) Man is a body (genus alone).

Key Takeaway
An incomplete hadd is a valid definition that optionally omits the near genus; it can use the differentia alone or with a distant genus.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

Verbal Definition: Clarifying Terms by Synonym
Author defines verbal definition as replacing an obscure word with a more famous synonym.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify a verbal definition and distinguish it from a real definition by checking whether it merely replaces a term with a more famous synonym without revealing essence.

Core Idea
Verbal definition swaps an obscure word for a common synonym—it does not give essence.

In Islamic sciences, we often encounter unfamiliar terms. Before we can define something in depth, we may need a simple verbal explanation—replacing the rare word with a well-known synonym. This lesson introduces verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi) and shows how it differs from real definition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obscure word (definiendum)
Look for the word that is unfamiliar to the intended audience. This is the term being defined.
In the example, 'birr' is the obscure word.
2
Find the synonym (muradif) provided
The definition gives a synonym that is more famous. Check if the synonym is indeed more widely known to the person being defined.
The synonym for 'birr' is 'wheat' (qamh).
3
Verify the audience condition
The definition must be more famous for the specific person (al-mu'arrif lahu). The same word may be obscure for one person and clear for another.
4
Distinguish from real definition
A real definition reveals the essence (genus and differentia) or at least describes properties. A verbal definition only clarifies the verbal meaning. Check if the definition gives genus/differentia; if not, it is verbal.
Defining 'birr' as 'wheat' is verbal; defining 'insan' as 'rational animal' is real.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما التعريف اللفظي: فهو تبديل لفظ خفي بلفظ مُرادف أشهر عند المعرف له ، كقولنا في تعريف البر: هو القمح، فإنه مرادف للبر أشهر منه لشهرة استعماله في ألسنة العامة والخاصة. (3) المعرف له هو الشخص الذي يذكر له التعريف ليتصور الشيء المعرف.
As for verbal definition (al-ta'rif al-lafzi): it is replacing an obscure word with a synonym more famous to the person being defined, as in our definition of 'birr': it is 'wheat', for it is a synonym for 'birr' more famous than it, due to the frequency of its usage in the tongues of the common and the elite. (3) The 'person being defined' (al-mu'arrif lahu) is the person for whom the definition is mentioned so that he may conceive the defined thing.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage defines 'verbal definition' (al-ta'rif al-lafzi). The author explains that it is simply replacing an unfamiliar word with a more well-known synonym. The example given is defining 'birr' (which can mean grain/wheat) as 'wheat' (qamh). Since 'qamh' is more commonly used among both the general public and specialists, it clarifies the meaning. The footnote (3) explains that 'al-mu'arrif lahu' is the person receiving the definition, who wants to conceive the defined thing. This type of definition does not reveal the essence or properties; it only clarifies the verbal meaning.

Key Terms
تعريف لفظي
المعرف له
مرادف

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Man is a rational animal.
B) Man is a laughing animal.

D) The world is temporally originated.

Key Takeaway
Verbal definition clarifies terminology without revealing essence, serving as a preliminary step in Islamic sciences.
